--- 帖子 #1 ---
UPDATE 26 Sept 2011 : I used in past years this ea in real account and deplated it very fast after few consecutive losses occurred !! So be advise that this trading system doesn't work in anyway under any market conditions and currency pairs used at least not in the long run (+2 years). Consider this thread only as a mere excercise to learn how to not trade forex market.

I'll not remove this first post so that other newbie trader (as I was at that time) can learn something from my errors.

Hi Firebirders !

I started here a new fresh thread about further improvement based on Firebird EA v0.63G engine that seems actually the best version ever made with incredible performance tested by a lot of users in old post.

I will try, as much as i can, to update regularly this first post so every news,settings,fix will be written here.

I wish to thanks to all users that in old thread help to improve Firebird in particular Mono for testing and sharing his result and setting to FF users.

[How it works Firebird ?]

(taken from EA code)
Firebird calculates a 10 day SMA and then shifts it up and down based on a percentage to form a channel.

For the calculation of this SMA either close (more trades) or H+L (safer trades) is used.

When the price breaks a band a postion in the opposite of the current trend is taken. If the position goes against us we simply open an extra position to average (pipstep function).

To avoid enter a trade while a strong trend is in place a divergence function is used that is calculated as difference between a Faster SMA (by default set to 23) and a Slower SMA (by default set to 84).

* Firebird v0.63g :

- Our loved EA  This version it seems to be a pips machine , implement pipstep to average position and divergence to avoid strong trend.

* Firebird v1.0a :

- Based on Firebird v0.63g engine.

- Fixed bug that prevent to all JPY pairs to enter often a trade due to a calculation error on divergence function.

- Removed looping print about Account Equity on Expert tab.

- Deleted override settings if you use TF30 timeframe chart.

*Firebird v1.0c (modified by Wackena)

- Average daily range calculated automatically using ATR on past 21 days, there is no more need to setup manually StopLoss,TakeProfit and Pipstep, they are all calculated automatically.

- Added Money Management routine. If you want to manually set lot size, set UseMM=0(false)

- Added MaxOpenOrders routine to add control as to max number of open orders at one time per pair. If not wanted, set MaxOpenOrders=10.

- Added Trailing stop function

[Firebird Settings (based on Mono's settings)]

- Firebird_settings_v1.0.zip : Contains two versions of preset files that seems  to works better :

1) Mono's fixed setting (Mono_settings_fixed_v1.0.zip): Fixed tp=30, sl=300, pipstep=30 for all pairs

2) Mono's variable setting (Mono_settings_variable_v1.0.zip) : different setting for each pair based on average daily range (in pips). Take profit (TP), Stop loss (LS) and PipStep are calculated with these formulas :
TP = Daily Avg Range*2/10 , SL = Daily Avg Range*2 , PipStep = Daily Avg Range/10

EUR/USD TP=22 SL=220 PIPSTEP=11 (Daily Avg Range = 110)

GBP/USD TP=30 SL=300 PIPSTEP=15 (Daily Avg Range = 150)

USD/CHF TP=25 SL=250 PIPSTEP=12 (Daily Avg Range = 125)

EUR/JPY TP=21 SL=210 PIPSTEP=10 (Daily Avg Range = 105)

USD/JPY TP=20 SL=200 PIPSTEP=10 (Daily Avg Range = 100)

USD/CAD TP=21 SL=210 PIPSTEP=10 (Daily Avg Range = 105)

AUD/USD TP=16 SL=160 PIPSTEP=8 (Daily Avg Range = 80)

EUR/CHF TP=10 SL=100 PIPSTEP=5 (Daily Avg Range = 50)

EUR/GBP TP=9 SL=90 PIPSTEP=5 (Daily Avg Range = 45)

AUD/JPY TP=15 SL=150 PIPSTEP=7 (Daily Avg Range = 75)

* Mono's chart time frame : M1 (1 minute chart)

--- 帖子 #25 ---
We need to have a tutorial on how to install and operate and EA. Anyhow the .set file should be in the Experts directory folder. You can put one there manually by using Windows Explorer or you can save one from the Firebird settings screen. To add firebird to the chart from the navigator menu simply drag it with your mouse to the chart. A settings window will come up. Make sure that "Allow Live Trading" is set under the "Common" Tab. The other tab you can edit the EA settings.

--- 帖子 #28 ---
skyline,

attached is Firebird_v1.0c with a routine added to auto-calculate variable settings. I followed Mono's calculation as you posted above. Backtest results comparing v.10a & v1.0c is attached. v1.0c did much better with almost 4 times more orders, but had several loses. Even with the loses, the overall profit was up.

This EA has 3 other routines added: UseMM which is a Money Management routine. If you want to manually set lot size, set UseMM=0(false). Another is a MaxOpenOrders routine to add control as to max number of open orders at one time per pair. If not wanted, set MaxOpenOrders=10. And the 3rd is a Trailing Stop routine. If not wanted, set TrailingStop=0.

Maybe a few members can forward test to see if results are better.

Also, I have posted Firebird_v1.0b on mr.trader's new thread at http://www.forexfactory.com/forexfor...33&postcount=8

This EA has a hedging routine added to help control high float sizes.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #39 ---
Ok. I will list the steps and you can see if yours are correct.

1. close MT4

2. right click on start button left corner. left click on explore.

3. Scroll down until you find program files and click on the + sign.

4. scroll down until you find your broker MT4 folder and click on the + sign

5. here in the experts folder is where you place the firebird EA. (not in the indicator folder)

6. Start your MT4 program back up.

7. Make sure you Navigator window is open on the left side, below the currency prices.

8. scroll thru the navagtor until you find the firebird EA.

9. Drag that EA into your chart window.

10. Right click in your chart window and select Expert Advisors and then select properties.

10. this will bring up the menu of settings.

11. You can adjust the settings to any that you have found in this thread or use your own.

12. select the common tab and make sure the Allow Live Trading is selected

13. press ok.

14. go to the top of the program and make sure that the menu tab for Expert Advisors shows a green arrow and not a red x. if the red x is present, just press the tab and it will go green.

15. You should now have a smiley face in the right hand corner of your screen.

Please ignore the steps you already know. I have no idea what your level is...

hope this helps...

--- 帖子 #41 ---
The way I did it is, got the daily high and low from july 04 til july 06, worked out the daily difference and then averaged it out.

AVG * 2 = SL

SL / 10 = TP & Pipstep

For the more adventurous

SL / 20 = pipstep

--- 帖子 #42 ---
We have come to the conclusion that in order to trade this EA safely you need $1000 per pair on a mini account. On a micro account I guess that would work out to $100 per pair. So if you have $300 then no more than 3 pairs. You might even want to start with 2 if you want to be really safe.

The broker is up to you. I use IBFX and so do many others. I have no experience with FXDD, but I've heard decent things about them.

If you open a mini account then leave the lot size as 0.1 (regular acct the lot should be 0.01 for a micro)

0.1 in a regular account is 1 mini lot, and in a mini account 0.1 is a micro lot.

Hope that helps.

Good luck with your test and live results if you go ahead with it.

--- 帖子 #59 ---
Doc,

Firebird was designed for slight trending, sine wave cyclic market. It is not that critical where order entry is made. It depends on the cyclic market going up & down. It makes most profits when it enter orders to go in the wrong direction. It uses the pipstep function to enter multiple orders with the assumption that market will retrace. The problem that has always existed with Firebird, is the big Stoploss needed to allow cyclic movement and the negative effect of news events. If several orders are open when news comes out, it's really a coin toss if the effect will be good or back. It is the concept from this forum that hedge orders (Firebird_v1.0b) and variable pair settings (Firebird_v1.0c) could help minimize news event effect. Time will tell with forward testing if these concepts are valid. What I can say for certain is, that you can't out think the market all of the time. If you are looking for the get rich quick scheme, in my opinion, this is not the way. If you looking to make a living or some extra money over the long haul, then doing your own Due Diligence is the way to go. Other people will not make money for you, only you will make money for you.

StopLoss is most useful in short sine wave cyclic conditions such as with jpy pairs. With gbp/usd type pair and its wider cyclic waves, StopLoss can prematurely close orders and thus not achieve max potential gains. I personally, would reccommend to carefully use Firebird on gbp/usd. This pair seems to have the longest cyclic trends and this is where excessive pipstep orders occur. I'm trading Firebird with a mini Live account and with gbp/usd, lot size =0.01, remaining pairs, 0.1 and above. Over time and market conditions, gbp/usd has most of the loses. This is not to say the other pairs don't have loses. I've had ouch times with usd/jpy and usd/chf, just not as many times as with gbp/usd.

Firebird_v1.0c can run on all currencies. Settings can be the same for all or individually set as per personal preference. Over the next few weeks, i hope feedback from members, who are forward testing, will report results to this forum. From that data, we may be able to determine  if perferred settings for a currency pair is needed.

I've been asked several times what pairs I trade. I trade 9 pairs. eur/usd, gbp/usd, usd/jpy. usd/chf, eur/jpy, eur/chf, usd/cad, aud/usd, gbp/jpy. No logic as to why these. I would recomment to demo as many as you feel comfortable with. This could 1 pair or all available.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #73 ---
Although the trailing stop was added to version c, it will not work sometime since it is included in the method "EnterPositionBasedOnOpen". This method will be only invoked when if MathAbs(diverge)<=DivergenceLimit. I think, the correct way to implement the trailing stop is to move the trailing stop out of the "if (MathAbs(diverge)<=DivergenceLimit)".

Thanks!

Scott

--- 帖子 #77 ---
If you are using v1.0c, the stoploss is calculated by the EA. What is entered in the inputs is overwritten by the EA. If control over Stoploss is needed, use v1.0a or 1.0b.

The descriptions of the EAs are on the threads where the EAs are posted,

Wackena

--- 帖子 #94 ---
Hi Mr.Trader

How much is actually your negative float balance ? Had you got a lot of loss in a row ?

That popup is written by EA in function LossCheck() when your loss is high so it alert you about that.

It's displayed when Last Account Equity (red from log file) less Actual Account Equity is more or equal to PipLoss (usually set to 500) * Lotsize (usually set to 0.1) , try to check this value to see if this condition is true.

hope this help you

--- 帖子 #101 ---
The "Excessive Loss" alert is when AccountEquity has loss value as set by the input PipsLoss=500 * Lot Size. You can turn the alert off by waiting and it will reset itself at end of day. 2nd by increasing the PipsLoss input value. Or, comment out the alert line in the code.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #152 ---
giapel,

This can be an annoyance. It does not effect trading at all. It was originally put in code to allow user to set a zone of time each day that was felt to be bad trading time and put this comment on the chart.  If you do not want to use it , set OpeningHour = 0 and ClosingHour = 23.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #155 ---
FB v1.0a trades 24 hours per day. The first order was placed using RVI indicator and then next 2 orders would be Pipstep orders. This EA works on reverse trending. This means it almost seems to enter 1st order in wrong direction, because it makes money by placing pipstep orders as it trends in wrong direction. Then when trend reverses, the pipstep and hopefully the first order are closed with profit. So far, with present settings, this seem to be happening very consistently.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #165 ---
Equity / Margin(used) = Margin Level

IBFX liquidates you when you hit 50%

FXDD when you hit 80%

To be safe this number should be higher than 150%, imho.

dee

--- 帖子 #166 ---
Attached are modified versions of 1.0a, 1.0b & 1.0c with a new input called MinMarginLevel. Enter minimum Margin Level % where trading stops below this level. Enter percent as whole numbers; such as 100, 250, 500 & etc.

I set the Margin Level equation as AccountEquity() / AccountMargin() and EA would not place orders. Journal message was divide zero. It took me a while to figure out that at the beginning AccountMargin() is 0. So, divide by zero error. I added 0.001 to AccountMargin() to get 1st trade and then the EA ran OK.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #169 ---
I had the same problem Wackena

I did resolve in this way :

Inserted Code  // Calculate Margin Level
double MarginLevel()
{
double fMarginLevel=0;

if (AccountMargin() > 0)
{
fMarginLevel = ((AccountEquity()/AccountMargin())*100);
}

return(fMarginLevel);
}

Anyway good work as always Wacky

Unfortunately i cannot modify anymore my first post to add your new versions,  i don't know why but this is really disappoint me

THeres only ONE BIG problem i find with the firebird EA. It overtrades. And when i say overtrade i mean it opens pointless positions based on nothing. IT has many winners, but the floating stuff is ridiculous. It will probably end up positive but really, to keep a realistic stop loss on this program you would get burnt so quick. I am going off someones recommendation of 120 pip stop loss. Now if i was to lose that trade, the win to loss is 6:1. Meaning 6 wins = 1 loss. Now its easy to keep this, but i mean 3 losses in a row =                    18 wins. Which is pretty much al the profit. Seems to be a break even strategy to me.

--- 帖子 #239 ---
Is this a co-incidence or what?.....Someone above is sending us signals.

Ok, this is what i'm upto.

We know that Firebird works great 90% of the time, but it needs assistance during trying times. (For the purpose of this explanation I'll call Firebird "Mr Firebird"). And in saying that I've got in the works, "Mrs Firebird".

Lets assume we are looking at GBPUSD with the following settings.

TP = 30

SL = 300

PIPSTEP = 15

Mrs Firebird see's what Mr Firebird is doing and protects and cleans up after him.

Basically she straddles him....(no pun intended)... when the price has moved TP in the opposite direction. As the price moves further away, she moves her SL to BE+1(no point in walking away with nothing).

When Mr Firebird gets Stopped out, her SL moves to where he got stopped and her TP will move to price +/- 30.

I hope your following me so far.

So I'm looking at running 2 EA's on 1 Account.

Also Mrs Firebird will be able to place BUY/SELL STOPS before news where MR Firebird is in a losing position.

e.g.  before news GBPUSD trade is at -250 pips. So Mrs Firebird places BUY/SELL STOPS at his -300 with tight trailstop.

Any thoughts?

--- 帖子 #284 ---
Find below in the code

if ( !(IsTesting() || IsDemo()) ) { if (LossCheck()) { Alert("excessive loss!"); PlaySound("alert.wav"); return(0); }} // included by Renato

And comment it out with //.

After you compile all your settings will be reset, so you will need to re-apply them.

if ( !(IsTesting() || IsDemo()) ) { if (LossCheck()) { Alert("excessive loss!"); PlaySound("alert.wav"); return(0); }} // included by Renato

//if ( !(IsTesting() || IsDemo()) ) { if (LossCheck()) { Alert("excessive loss!"); PlaySound("alert.wav"); return(0); }} // included by Renato

Notice the // in front of the line, it comments it out.

--- 帖子 #304 ---
I've noticed that several people are getting similar yet different results from F.B.  This difference at times may be attributed to the pipstep value.  Can someone tell me what this pipstep value represents and what its function is with respect to Firebird?

Thanks,

Alan

--- 帖子 #305 ---
Pipstep is the value where a new order is opened if the trade is going against you. So if you have a pipster of 20 and the trade goes in the negative by 20 pips a new trade is open in the same direction.

--- 帖子 #306 ---
When Firebird takes a position it assumes that the 'trend' reverses very soon.

If it doesn't retrace with in PipStep pips then add another lot and average the position. When the position is averaged this way there is a higher probabilty that the ProfitTarget is met.

So PipStep controls how soon/often a position is averaged.

To small is your position grows very quickly.

To small it averages to slow and reduces your chances.

--- 帖子 #312 ---
If it was that simple I would set it to 9999. And then remove it completly...

Example:

1] PipStep=30, ProfitTarget=30

2] Enter Short at 1.0000

3] Price moves up to 1.0030 -> add an extra lot

4] Average price is now 1.0015

5] Price goes to 0.9975 and then goes up to 1.2222

6] That price passes 0.9985 (1.0015-0.0030) so there we grab profits.

1] PipStep=50, ProfitTarget=30

2] Enter Short at 1.0000

3] Price moves up to 1.0030 -> no 50 pips so no averaging

5] Price goes to 0.9975 and then goes up to 1.2222

6] We need 1.0000-0.0030=0.9970

7] No we are in big trouble because the trend goes up to 1.2222. A heavy drawdown

--- 帖子 #316 ---
Alan,

What's best I can't tell you. But you understand you have to find an

equilibrium. So you know what to work toward.

Take a look at:

extern double IncreasementType =0;//0=just add every PipStep, >0 =OrdersToal()^x *Pipstep

You can use that input to create variable PipSteps.

Look in the Firebird document for more details but decreasing PipStep

may help your cause.

I don't have the same mind set as many here. I wouldn't even considered

M1. For me preserving capital is the #1 aim.

Some risk controlling things the coder may consider.

Run Firebird on 10 pairs but allow only 2/3 pairs to be trading simultaneously.

Use uncorrelated pairs.  http://www.mataf.net/en/analysis-correlation.htm

When a pair average for the 3rd time set max open pairs to 1 and TakeProfit to zero

Waiting for a trade to go your way can cost money to. Say you earn $100/day. But you refuse to take $300 losing trade and wait 10 days to exit with a $100 profit. That trade earned you $100, but kept you out of 9 trades worth $900. So you 'lost' $900. My point is that admitting defeat might be better.

It's better to make 50% a month with little drawdown than 100% with more risk. Look at it with compounding.

If you make a nice percentage your account quickly doubles with means faster profits etc.

An added bonus you can sleep at night instead of worrying about DD.

Hi,

Thanks for great work by Wackena and others. In Post 91, Wackena mentioned a bug in version b as

This seems not fixed in the newer version b. In this version b, hedge orders will still only be placed on initial sells. The bug is, in the code, the value of variable ret will never be 2 before "Go SHORT". so it will never place the hedge buy order for initial sells. I tried to use another two if statements after open initial orders (including sells and buys) before the return, the issue seems gone.

Perhaps, Wackena already found the bug and fixed it.

--- 帖子 #361 ---
I think Mono explained somewhere that the news isn't what causes the problem, it's the open positions.  They could be a week, two weeks old or more.  You can't get rid of this without destroying profitability and probably the probability of it even working.  It's inherent to the function of Firbird.  It could probably just as easily go for you as against you, so I see no reason to change it during the news.   Is there something I'm missing?

You have to be willing to accept drawdowns in any system, but even more so in an entirely mechanical automated system.  These drawdowns really only seem to signal "Profit!, Straight ahead!" to me.   I think in the other thread someone described how to envision Firebird as something that takes advantage of the markets tendency to return to average, - like a stretched rubber band - the further off it is, the harder it will snap back.  And snag profit along the way.

Just to clarify Labrat, I'm not neccessarily directly addressing you, but the situation in general.  Just don't want to come off preachy.

--- 帖子 #372 ---
Finally had time to review Firebird v1.0b1 to correct reason why EA was only placing hedge order on main sell orders. Attached is FB v1.0b2. This EA will placed 1 hedge order for each Buy or Sell main orders.  Also to control number of open orders, this EA has input OpenOrders. This sets the number of main orders opened for each chart. Eaxmple if = 2, max open orders will range 0-4. If = 3, range will be 0-6 max open orders.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #412 ---
Currently, in all FB versions, there is no trace for error messages when failed in sending orders. So we could not see why there are no trades opening.

To catch the error, I made following changes to the FireBird:

1) Included the header file stdlib.mqh to the FB at the first line.<STDLIB.MQH>

2) for Sell order,

int ticket=OrderSend(Symbol(),OP_SELL,Lots,Bid,slip,Bid+(Stoploss*Point),Bid-(TakeProfit*Point),GetCommentForOrder(),MagicNumber,0,clOpenSell); // modified by Renato

if(ticket>0) {

Print("Opened Sell order.");

} else {

err = GetLastError();

Print("Error opening Sell order (",err,"): ",ErrorDescription(err));

}

3)For Buy order:

int ticket = OrderSend(Symbol(),OP_BUY,Lots,Ask,slip,Ask-(Stoploss*Point),Ask+(TakeProfit*Point),GetCommentForOrder(),MagicNumber,0,clOpenBuy); // modified by Renato

if(ticket>0) {

Print("Opened Buy order.");

} else {

err = GetLastError();

Print("Error opening Buy order (",err,"): ",ErrorDescription(err));

}

After added such error trace code, we may see why there are no trades.

For example, I got another error:

2006.08.28 05:47:40 FireBird_v63 USDJPYm,M1: Error opening BUY order (4109): trade is not allowed.

But I do not understand why such error would happen.

Thanks!

Just an observation here on backtesting EA's using different brokers.  I use both SBFX and FXDD, and have demo accounts with both (live only with FXDD).  Last night I was backtesting different scenarios using FB 1.0a on both, and noticed that I was getting VASTLY different results with only slightly different settings.  I then set both EA's to exactly the same settings, and for exactly the same time period and backtested (using every tick option as usual).  The results weren't even in the same order of magnitude!!  I also noticed that FXDD used more than three times as many bars in the backtest than did SBFX.  I checked and rechecked that everything was set the same, and it was.  The only conclusion I can make on this is that FXDD has a better data set for backtesting.

Any other comments on this??

Doug

--- 帖子 #432 ---
I'm still working on it.

I really need help on coming up with the different variables.   The people that have  studied the statements  can probably  be of most help.  I'm really kinda shooting in the dark with these, some may be unnecessary or obviously faulty.  I need to know which settings logically have merit.  Otherwise, I'm afraid we're going to have too many combinations to properly test.

The global ones (accross all versions) I've come up with so far are:

1.  Time Period (on the chart)

2.  Pairs - Here's on I need help on.

I think that we should use different setups with the top 2,

top 4,6,8, and 10 pairs.  I've ordered the pairs from 1-10 based on

ATR, but is that the best way?  Should we number them according to

risk, win ratio, what?

3.  Brokers

4.  MA Length

5.  MA Timeframe

6.  MA Type

With 4,5, and 6, we're talking hundreds, or maybe thousands, of

permutations.

7.  Percent

Do we need to use different TP,SL,Pipstep settings too?  Cause now we're talking even more.  What about trading times?  Do we need to set it to only trade in certain hours for some of the tests?

There's a section of the code dealing with divergence, iFX Analyzer I believe, that has multiple settings too (fast period/price, slow period/price).  Do those warrant manipulation?

Then there are the settings exclusive to the multiple versions themselves, which shouldn't add too much to the complexity, so I've been saving them for last.

As if this weren't enough, we should probably run 2 or 3 of each setup allowing one to run unhindered, one reset every week, the other reset every other week.

I'm sure there are some more I haven't even come up with yet.

I hope everyone understands the magnitude of this.  This would be completely overwhelming to try all the permutations I've outlined already, much less the ones I haven't. --- 帖子 #444 ---
Yes, there is a difference.

The MA_time sets up the envelope in which Firebird executes trades, some people like a setting of 30 others 15.

Placing Firebird on the 1Min chart helps with divergence, in other words spikes. If there is a spike in the 1min bar, it will not open a new trade until it subsides.

--- 帖子 #445 ---

--- 帖子 #446 ---
Finally, I found why sometimes there is no trades (when it should be).

There is a bug in this version caused by following code:

double value = iATR(NULL,PERIOD_D1,21,0);

if(Point == 0.01) value = value*100;

if(Point == 0.0001) value = value*10000;

TakeProfit = value*2/10;

Stoploss = value*2;

PipStep = value/10;

Sometimes, the iATR returns value of zero, this results in the zero of parameters TakeProfit, Stoploss and PipStep.

This can clearly seen when you add following Print statment to the code and recompile it:

Print ("Value from iATR is: ", value);

You will see sometimes the value is really zero. Certainly, it causes failure in OrderSend because of invalid stop, invalid price, etc.

In my previous post, I suggested to add error trace for OrderSend, and I got various error such as

Error opening Sell order (130): invalid stops.

Please keep in mind the problem only happens when Daily True Average Range is zero. Because of this bug, the test of this version would be unrealiable.

Thanks!

--- 帖子 #455 ---
There are 3 sets of hours.

a] What you see on the clock in your home.

b] Server time. -> What you see on the chart.

c] Time of the market.

a] is not relavant.

You have to align b and c.

13:00 NY 'stockmarket time' could be 07:00 broker time.

Because MT4 uses chart/server/broker time you have to enter 07:00 not 13:00

--- 帖子 #471 ---
trituetrade,

Once you drag the EA to the chart, there are two things (minimum) you need to do.  First, right click on the mouse, choose 'expert advisors', properties, common tab, and check off the button to allow for live trading.  Second, you have to hit the "Expert Advisors" button on the toolbar.  At this point in time, a smiley face will (should) appear in the top right corner.

This is the same process for either a demo or a live account.  Once you do this, you can adjust the settings, or 'inputs' on the EA.

Doug

--- 帖子 #479 ---
That's easy with Firebird.

But don't be suprised that suddenly it takes back all those millions.

I would advise 2 hours looking at a chart with the envelope plotted on it.

Set up a chart with a envelope so that 95% of the prices stay in the channel. Then look at the places where price breaks the channel and what happens next.....

I've been to long away from Firebird (and this thread) to know what changed in the code, but from what I've read Hendrick is aware of the drawdown issue and is trying to fix it.

v1.x seems to have hedging. That's certainly a good risk control too.

There are to many versions to judge but I noticed that the original rules are broken on at least one versions.

When PipStep is reached a position is added but not averaged.

Averaging makes the chances of winning higher/faster.

So it will reduce the float.

This is just demo trading but in real trading I would like to suggest some other way of burning cash

Trade on as many uncorrelated pairs as possible (size down) trade on as many time frames/settings as possible. The aim is to get uncorrelated trades.

Meaning that they move independantly. If all all pairs get hit by a drawdown the float gets high. When market conditions return to 'normal' all positions cash in. IF you didn't get a margin call.

If everything is uncorrelated profit roll in gently and constantly.

With correlated settings you build up a lake of potential profits that gets cashed in one lucky day. The only profit is the one in your account. So I prefer the uncorrelated approach...

That's are the reasons why I don't trade Firebird. (but still see potential for it)

Rember we are trying to steal pips from the big banks with zillions of resources, 1000's of full time analysts and 100's of number crunching mainframes.

It won't be easy!

Well, according to my back testing Firebird may not die, but it certainly may look like a lame duck for extended periods. Took me awhile to get around to it, but I've finally managed to test 3 of better performing pairs lately... EUR/USD, USD/CAD, and USD/JPY back to 12/1/2004. Not that back testing is everything, but I think the larger the time frame (due to more data points), the better idea how a system is likely to behave... at least as long as my test data is good, which I have no idea. (got it from http://www.alpari-idc.com/en/dc/databank.php )

I did my testing with the current popular settings (T/P = 30, S/L = 300 on the 1 minute chart, etc.). The results show a slow bleed from 12/04 - 6/05. It may be longer but my data doesn't go back any further.

I'm not sure what changed about the market conditions in June '05, but it must have been significant because results are definitely different from June 05' - present. And the difference seems to affect all three pairs similarly (probably because they're USD based). I'm thinking that whatever conditions contributed to Firebirds poor performance during that time are likely to come around again. Maybe soon.

Right now, my opinion is that this is a good EA in that it doesn't seem to lose money when left alone (many do), but over the long haul it isn't going to take anyone from "rags to riches". I do think that returns can be improved with smart manual intervention, but those improvements will be incremental not exponential. I hope this doesn't pour cold water on anyone's party... And it is my hope that somebody can provide different/better back test results that will refute my tests.

Edit: Got a little more data back to 6/04. Will add this to my testing...

Edit # 2:  After some more testing, I have a pretty good suspicion the test data from Alpari is FUBAR'd prior to 10/05, so forget I said anything. ;-)

I've been lurking a little bit.

I have a suggestion on the issue about closing down the EA before news, etc. The EA would still manage stop losses, so, your positions should exit if it goes against you. It would also manage TP as well, if the news is with you.

It seems that the biggest concern about news trades is opening new positions either because of the news, or just before the news.

Instead of closing everything down, why not just have a boolean flag that tells Firebird to not make any new orders. Turn the flag on a day before a big news event. Turn it off a day after the news.

--- 帖子 #509 ---
Yardie,

The same is here, concerning one of my tests on the 15 minutes time frame the negative float is greater than the profit having the test running for 1.5 weeks.

I think the reason for this is that when hedging Firebird 1.0b versions open two market orders (one buy and one sell) at the same time. So one of the buy or sell orders will always go against us meanwhile the other goes to profit. But one of the two orders will remain there for long and increase the float, particularly in a trending market. According to the best case scenario first the first one then the other takes profit, but in the worst case scenario the first one then the other will stop out - depending on the market movement.

Other strategies, such as news trading straddle EAs, open pending orders both sides of trade (buy and sell). Once the first pending order has been activated the other side is liquidated and the positive is used to go to profit direction. This way only one order will be activated and in a trending market it probably goes to the profitable direction and the float can be retain on a reasonable level.

--- 帖子 #510 ---
This is a good point. Maybe we need to make a variation of this version and compare the two. The new version would close out or liquidate the other order once one side was activated. I think that this would help the float also. Any other thoughts on this? Is there anyone willing to program this change?

--- 帖子 #514 ---
There are some debate on whether FB can handle breaking news, if you look at the nature of FB is to take small profit during normal spike along the trend or ranging market. But breaking news may wipe out the gain profit in a short time of trading. Take for an example of setting 30-300-30 method with one currency.

If there are 5 trades where 2 are closed trade with 30 pips profit, 1 trade with 15 pips in progressiive profit and the other 2 trades in 10 pips loss as float. When the breaking news come out, either up or down heavily with surprise to the market. That is the market may swing more than 300 pips.

If the existing trade is in favor to the news, then the 3 trades will conclude with another 90 pips in total which give a total of 150 pips for 5 trades. But for the other way round, the existing 3 trades will give 900 pips loss and the nett loss is 840 pips.

Hence my point is it may be good to close all the trades before the breaking news.

--- 帖子 #515 ---
As I mentioned in my earlier post, FB is performing bound scalping for the small profit during the normal spike. It doesn't matter for the market in ranging but not for trend market.

In trend market, the price can start from small pips until the top trend of say 400 pips. Take up trend as an example, if FB trade short when there is a spike for take profit environment in the initial trend. Then that trade will not close when the trend is heading upward until SL is hit. This is why some member do encounter a SL of 300 pips 20 days later.

Hence my suggestion is 1:3 ratio or not more than 1:5 ratio should be used instead of 1:10 ratio.

--- 帖子 #523 ---
I don't see how a hedge can cause a extra float.

Besides the costs for buying lots needed for building the hedge everything should even out AFTER the building of the hedge.

When the hedge is build when the float is -300 pips that float will never increase because the profit and loss from thereon will even out.

But the situation can last a long time. Assume it takes 2 months to return to the right level. That would be 2 months of tied up money.

Say the hedge saves you 500 pips in losses but also keeps you out of 800 pips of gains because it tied up all your funds we still are on negative ground.

The only ways around that are no hedge or try to detect the reversal point.

Drop the hedge (profit) then wait for the TP. Float increases again but you have profits also locked in.

An aditional problem is whipsaws. Like always....

--- 帖子 #524 ---
TraderSeven,

You are right the profit and loss from hedge will even out - but only till one of the orders reaches TP. After that the reamaining order increases the float for a while.

--- 帖子 #527 ---
I assume the hedge has no TP so it are the original orders that have the TP hit. If my assumption is correct I think dropping the hedge should be done more intelligently.

Say we hit -300 and thats our point we build a hedge.

We get hit by another 1000 pips but the hedge evens that out

After that 1000 pips price goes back in our favour and moves to our TP of 30 pips. The hedge gets dropped. Is that how it works now?

Ideally the hedge should be dropped at that 1000 pip mark. It cashes in 1000 pips. The float will suddenly jump 1000 pips. But in a way it's still hedged by the 1000 pips in your account so in a way it's still hedged. And more importantly it stops a margin call.

On top of that we collect the normal profits.

It's hard/impossible to detect that turning point but I think the aim should be cashing in on the hedge too.

--- 帖子 #534 ---
TraderSeven,

Thank you for your reply, you have some very good points.

If the hedging worked as you wrote it down, then the float would not increase. But I think now the hedge orders work on the same way as the normal orders, that is, using the settings of 30-300-30 and assuming the market goes to one direction for 300 pips, taking only one hedge order into consideration, there will be 30 pips profit and 300 pips loss, the balance is -270 pips. During the way to 300 pips, until we reached the first 30 pips the two orders even out but beyond 30 pips the negative  float will increase.

The ideal case would be if the market turned back right after 30 pips and would go back 60 pips from there giving us the possibility to take out the other 30 pips profit. So, a ranging market is advantegeous for this trading system.

Getting back to the example above, in reality, I think (but am not sure) hitting the first 30 pips and taking profit initialises another hedge order and so on and so on. Consequently, when we reach 300 pips we will have 10*30 pips profit (leaving the spread out of the calculation) and 9 pieces of floating losses: at -30; -60; -90; ... -270 and a 300 pips loss. At this case the net balance is zero and the negative float is 1350 when we reach the milestone at 300 pips.

If I was right, a trending market would be disasterous with this model.

Using pending orders instead of market orders when hedging and keeping live only the "right" half of the hedge pair and going along that 300 pips route we could reach 7*30 pips profit and would have 10 pips positive float assuming the gap were 10 pips at each order (300 = 8*10 gap + 7*30 profit + 10 float).

Any advice would be appreciated.

--- 帖子 #565 ---
The version set the TakeProfit dynamically using the following code:

double value = iATR(NULL,PERIOD_D1,21,0);

if(Point == 0.01)   value = value*100;

if(Point == 0.0001) value = value*10000;

TakeProfit = value*2/10;

Stoploss = value*2;

PipStep = value/10;

the value may be very small, sometimes, it can be 0. I have posted this problem for a few times but no one paid attention to it. If it is zero, it will not even open trades for you.

--- 帖子 #590 ---
forex4syg,

I read your previous post when you posted it. I just got caught up in some other things and forgot to respond.

I agree, there will be times when there will be error 130 (Invalid stops) due to calculated StopLoss being too low. If sl value is too close to or between the spread, server will not accept order. If StopLoss=0, trade will process OK. A 3-5 pips buffer could be added to Stoploss to stop this error 130. At this point, it does not seem to adversely effect the performance of the EA. I'm not sure, but it might even prevent entry into questionable trades.

Sorry for not responding sooner.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #594 ---
Hi Wackena,

Thanks a lot for your work.

I have noticed that when Stoploss is zero, there will be error in opening trade. Please correct me if am wrong. In the code, for example,

OrderSend(Symbol(),OP_SELL,Lots,Bid,slip,Bid+(Stoploss*Point),Bid-(TakeProfit*Point),GetCommentForOrder(),MagicNumber,0,clOpenSell); // modified by Renato

If parameter Stoploss is zero (resulted from the daily iATR), then Bid+(Stoploss*Point) = Bid, it is the same as the sell price. The order will be prevented. I think this is the reason why some people noticed that in the version c, there may be less orders opened at the beginning. Good or not, I do not know.

Do you have idea why daily ATR would even return zero?

I also noticed that in trailing stop, the fixed pips of 5 (below Bid or above Ask) in StopLoss would fail for some platform, for example, with NorthFinance, the trailing stop often does not work well because of invalid stop.

Thanks

--- 帖子 #595 ---
The possibility, but not likely, is the mathematical average of High minus Low over previous 21 bars (days) = 0. More likely for error 130, ATR <5.

I use the 5 pips gap for setting new s/l in t/s modify orders in EAs. Most other t/s codes that I have seen, set new s/l at the present s/l below Bid for Buy order and above Ask for Sell order. This sets the first new s/l from t/s function very close to order entry price. If price reverses and triggers s/l, usually it is very low profit. So I changed it to a fix 5 pips. This way if t/s is trigger, s/l is set nearer actual price to take more profit on reverses.

I haven't been monitoring for invalid stop as a result of this 5 pips gap. So far,  on IBFX live and demo, FDXX demos and North Finance demos, this t/s function has worked very well for me.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #607 ---
KingForex very true.

Therein lies my big concern over going live with Firebird.

Take cable for example. Price is historically quite high at the moment around 1.9000 and the market has been fairly flat for a while.

Say we start a trend south and price moves 100 to 150 pips in a day. Firebird will buy every 20 or 30 pips depending on your setting.

Would you close all trades? Of course not. You would expect price to reverse (just like after NFP) and give Firebird more winners.

But what if price goes south again the next day and keeps going. OK max trades limits buys to 10 trades per currency but some of us are using 5 to 7 pairs. So you have 10 buy orders that stop out at -300 over lets say 5 pairs. That will give you a total of -15,000 pips.

It has happened many times before - ask Traderseven the author of the EA. I myself have tested 63g since March and twice all my profits (and more) have disappeared when a major trend started.

So just be aware before you go live. The old Firebird weakness is still there waiting to bite.

--- 帖子 #678 ---
I don't have the slightest clue of how to program this, but here's my idea for detecting a trending market in regards to firebird. Have firebird look at the past 96 hours in one hour increments and have it compare the highest high vs the lowest low. To get the answer to the question of if we're in a trend or not, we have FB compute the percentage change in over all price between the high and low. If the cumulative total is say +.75% from ninety six hours ago, firebird goes into silent mode not placing trades until the percentage differential comes back down to say .5%. If the largest deviation occurs in less than say thirty six hours, we let firebird roam, but if the deviation is taking place and growing between thirty six to ninety six hours, we have firebird dive again until the time is right to surface. This is obviously just a rough sketch so far, so please do give some opinions on the idea.

BK, the latest versions can be found at Accrete's resource page.

Hi Accrete,

I still think the main issue concerning v1.0b2 version is that it places market orders so one half of the hedge always remains. Mainly in trending market the remaining half causes heavy float then losses in worse cases, I mean if the trend is strong.

My earlier posts regarding this issue where I detailed my idea:
http://www.forexfactory.com/forexfo...3&postcount=510
http://www.forexfactory.com/forexfo...5&postcount=522
http://www.forexfactory.com/forexfo...6&postcount=525
http://www.forexfactory.com/forexfo...1&postcount=535

My point is that pending orders would be more advantageous than market orders because this way the EA would put orders only to the trend direction.

--- 帖子 #689 ---
I been reading the posts about possible changes to the v1.0b (Hedge) EA.

Attached is v1.0b3 with following changes.

1. UseHedge- If=true, the hedge order is placed when pipstep step order is triggered. Separate inputs for HedgeTakeProfit & HedgeStoploss.

if=false, EA is v1.0a.

2.UseDayClose- If true, CloseLoosingTrades subroutine is activated to close loosing orders below input LossLevel on DayClose (0-sun, 1=mon, 2=tues, 3=wed, 4=thurs. 5=fri) and DayHour (LocalTime). For those that want to close loosing orders on Friday or before news events. To close all orders, LossLevel should be 5 pips above TakeProfit or HedgeTakeProfit setting (whichever is highest).

3. OpenOrders- Max open orders per currency pair. To trade as v1.0a, set this to 10.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #697 ---
Wondering if we ought to start another thread related to this, or if perhaps it's too broad a subject to bother covering within the parameters of the Firebird EA...

But the question is, how are we going to spot the big nasty trend?  We all know it's coming, and that it is going to do serious damage to our Firebird accounts.  This situation reminds me of watching those shows about killer asteroids... ;-)  Except in our case, I think we can expect this scenerio to occur once or more within the next several months.

With all that in mind, I am hoping to start a discussion specifically aimed at protecting our Firebird accounts from the "big nasty".

Here is what I've observed so far:

Through back testing, as well as a fundamental understanding of what it takes to "obey" a system, I do not condone closing trades early or arbitrarily closing everything on Friday.  None of the testing I've done indicates this is a good procedure.  I've tried closing everything weekly and monthly, but both yeild significantly less profit, and not much less in the way of loss.  The manual intervention I've had the most success with consists of simply turning Firebird off occasionally and letting the floating trades play themselves out.

But all this is a bit "nebulous" for my taste.  We have a concrete ruleset in place of executing trades (obviously), so it would be great to have set rules pertaining to the management of Firebird in general.  Perhaps trading pairs should be individually shut down when a certain fib level is reached, or when a particular candlestick pattern is observed on the daily chart.  Anyone else working on ideas in this direction?

--- 帖子 #708 ---
Accrete, et al

As I also said before, I agree with this approach and think it's worth pursuing with V1.0b2. Maybe we could call it V 1.0b3.

I also have another thought on this but with an earlier version. Hendrick in post #258 & #260 @ http://www.forex-tsd.com/expert-advi...d-v63g-26.html created Firebird v63H (with a correction in post 260) to v63H02. This may have also been posted @ FF as well, but I don't know where. Anyway, as is explained in the post quote:

"This setting is based on the idea that Firebird is doing well in a flat market, but could go wrong when the market gets volatile. The indicator (Firebirdv63H_IND) gives you an idea how this function works (you don’t need to attach this indicator to your charts for Firebirdv63H to work). The indicator is quite simple: it takes the values of the built-in indicators “ Bulls Power” and “ Bears Power” and adds them together. When these powers are in balance it’s safe to trade. When Bulls or Bears get the upper hand their sum crosses a certain level (until now I think levels of 40 and -40 works well) and Firebird isn’t allowed to place trades."

My understanding of this is that its' purpose is to prevent trades in volatile markets. My idea is to use this idea in conjunction with V1.0b2 while combining it with hedging orders but leaving them as pending orders to be cancelled once the trend is established. The "Safe Area" prevents orders during volatility and the "pending orders" go with the trend and are entered or their hedges are cancelled.

Any thoughts on this. Anyone willing to program something like this...? Wakena, what do you think?

1Trader2

P.S. V 63H02 as well as the Firebird Safe Indicator are posted on the above web site.

H02 has a "safe zone" area determined by Bulls and Bears.  Default is 40.  It won't trade if the price is out of the "safe zone".  Might help on trending markets.

--- 帖子 #751 ---
I setup v1.0c1 to go live on a small account last night and had some promising results for its first day.

I am trading this version on three pairs (EUR/USD, USD/JPY, & USD/CHF).

The only change that I made to the default settings was to change the Percent variable to 0.025. I had done a bit of backtesting and found this number to be very profitable. It places the orders fairly close together and seems to raise the odds of them hitting the T/P number.

Today's (9/6/2006) Record

19 Wins and 0 Losses

Total Booked Pips = 238

Total Floating Pips = -140

So basically it is a +98 Pip day. Not bad for a first day.

Tightening the band by using the smaller percent setting of 0.025 seems to also act as a bit of a hedge as their seems to be a nice balance of orders set on each side as the small swings happen.

I will post an update on tommorrows progress.

Just wanted to post a few thoughts here...

The last few pages have been everyone complaining about the recent "trend".  Myself, I just see a half day spike that is already starting to retrace (and has banked 4 TP trades this morning).  Now, if the prices continue for the next several days without any retraces...I'm in trouble, as is anyone lse running this live.  But, as I said, all we have had is a spike.  Maybe slower than a news spike, but a spike none the less.

I have yet to have any trade hit a S/L, so I am happy in that regard.

I was considering trying the H02 version, but after reading how it tries to protect from trends...it won't help much.  From what I found, it will stop opening new trades if it hits a S/L.  However, new losing trades will continue to be opened until that first S/L is hit.  Therefore, with the seemingly popular 30-300-30 settings, you will still have up to 10 losing trades...

Anyways...personaly, I have no intention of stopping the EA in the current market, and will ride out this recent market move.  If things work out, everything will retrace and bank me a whole lot of pips...if not, then all I can hope for is some good fluctuations to at least make some pips on the way to a S/L.

Just thought I would add my $0.02 (closer to $0.05...)

Chris

--- 帖子 #802 ---
Open the terminal window if not open. Click the 'account history' tab. In the window right mouse click over one of the closed trades that are displayed. Select 'save as detailed report' from the right click menu. Last go to the directory where you saved the report and zip the files you want to post.

--- 帖子 #808 ---
Been live 3 weeks now with good ole' V63G, and I'm quite happy with the results.  Like Cthauber, I'm running the 30-300 settings with % = .1.  Even with the current conditions, none of my stops even look close to being hit.

However, as many of us have commented in the past, I think this EA needs "managing" just like any trading tool, and that a traders success (or lack thereof) will be in line with their success as a trader in general.

My management has consisted strictly of turning the EA on or off at certain times based on what I see in the market and the nature or direction of my float (not necessarily the amount of float...).  I still think that closing any winning position early is a bad idea, and closing a losing position early is bad 99% of the time.  The pairs I've chosen are EUR/USD, USD/CAD, and sometimes USD/JPY.  I thought about including USD/CHF, but IMO it behaves too similarly to EUR/USD so I left it out.

Even with the EA turned on 90% of the time, float has never exceeded 15% of my account.  I'm currently @ +1140 pips (+27%) with ~340 pips float.  Based on what I have ascertained from the market, I hope most of the float will be "flushed" out positively soon.

Hello Birders,

This week firebird show us his teeths....

I run firebird to on two live acounts (63G), one without GBP, means without a drawdown, the outher with GBP, so i had a sl. Two long positions are still open and near the SL...  But my problem is not realy a big one, i hedged the GBP at 1.8780 with double lotsize from the 3 open buy positions... so i´m still in profit with the GBP...

But we should fix the "trendproblem" from firebird if he should perform well on the long run... With the actual versions (maybe not "b" versions, but i also don´t trust them) this bird garanteed wiped out our accounts if a strong major trend starts  !

So this is my idea...

Firebird is a counter trend EA, this means he opens positions when a long/short run is over in the outher direction... ok, that we know...

B U T  (!!!)

we also know from all our Demo and Live testing that near 95% of all postions get a 2nd, 3rd or more pipstep order... ok, that also means when we change the entry direction we alsways (remember near 95% ) get minimum one winning trade in trend direction...

I know, some of you think i´m a litle stupid, there are "b" versions what make exactly what i write,  and i  say they are flase...

W H Y (???)

Don´t forget, the main calculation for the entrys is still counter trend, so it´s not the same at all !!

We should anyway test it. Just change the entry  side,  when  Firebird goes  long, the "Trendbird" should go short and vince versa. If we have an complete EA witch works that way we can test it and use different settings for entry in trend direction, so we can change MA-length, MA-type, Percentage, Trailning Stop... and so on, only for this EA who opens in trend direction....

Think about it, if you let both EA´s run on the same account and the same pairs you will gain double in sideway markets and be hedged from the beginning when major trends starting....

I hope somebody have enough coding experience to code this so we can test next week !

Thanks for your help,

--- 帖子 #834 ---
Hi all!

last week was a really bad week for most of us...especially for the ones who put his or her hard-earned dinero to trade firebird.

I know most of us prefer a fully automated trading, I do too!, and we should keep exploring for better solutions...but for the meantime I think we can make a good use of more manual means of protecting your account if it really works.

For most with a lot of floating loss right now, open long GBP/USD positions are what is bringing the float up and also that is what is potentially really hazardous to your account. A coming move down South 100 pips should get you at least 500 to 1000 pips of loss, shouldn't it?

Here comes the interesting part, what if you could tell a couple of days ago there was a probable 280 pips move South coming after moving 130 or so pips move in the same direction?  Off course, you could bail out with a lot less loss at that point, could'nt you?

In fact, we could predict the move and prevent the major loss that happened this week if we knew what Moutekitrader (one of our fellow menbers at FF) is generously sharing in his thread "Mouteki Trading".
http://www.forexfactory.com/forexfor...ead.php?t=7883

I was thinking about the same thing when one of my open position was floating around 5 to 10 pips below the TP.

Different broker uses different server time hence different chart data but I feel some people get totally different result from using exact same setting on the firebird. I would not be surprised if that is due to the degree of manipulation on the brokers' parts...I didn't type it but my fingers did!

But seriously, that can add more profitability to firebird but there's one problem with not setting TP and SL at the server. When, for some reason, we can't connect to the server...lost internet connection, virus attack, broker's server disrupted, for example...our accounts would be very vulnerable to sudden market moves. We cannot say with certainty the market cannot move 1,000 pips in one day in any situation...even with reasonable S/L that would be a margin call time anyway though  .

Unless brokers are manupulating manually, what can work would be something like this: Firebird initially sets T/P at 100 pips but when the price reaches at 30 pips in the money, it closes the position immediately.

Firebird initially sets S/L at 350 pips but when the price reaches 300 pips againt the position, it closes the position immediately.

It all depends on how brokers, potentially, manipulate the price but what do you guys think?

Closing positions randomly depending on the momentum of the move may be more sophisticated solution if brokers can outsmart us using the above tricks.

Cheers.

100 winning trades to equal ten losing trades!!!

--- 帖子 #872 ---
Hi there, yes the bug on the "Reverse" FB is there, it happens to be a simple duplicate comma , ....that's it. So you can double click on the error line when you try to compile it and you will see the obvious error.

Now, what you can do also is take your favorite version and just reverse it yourself. Very easy to do. Here is a paste of a post i made over at tsd this morning:

After fixing the small extra comma error in the above posted reverse FB i went ahead and tested it in demo today on another version of FB head to head with a normal. They both tripped trades in opposite directions on the EUR in the normal, and CAD on the reverse in harmony on seperate MT4 accounts. Interesting to watch. The FBrev closed out 3 trades at 18pips with +1 float as i post, and the normal closed 29+ with -45 pips...funny stuff this FireBird. But at least we know a simple code switcherooo does what we told it to.

snip of code change, just copy paste the lines from the "BUY" and put them in place of the "SELL" code. I just commented out the original lines " // " so the original was still there for future referrence. Remember you will do this switch on each area your version takes a trade. Some will have several, so look for them all. Here is an example paste from one of these areas inside the FB version i used for my test this morning:

if((myMA*(1+Percent/100))<BID (Bid && Direction!="22">=(LastPrice+(CurrentPipStep*Point)) || myTotal==0) ) // Go SHORT -> Only sell if >= 30 pips above previous position entry

{

OrderSend(Symbol(),OP_BUY,Lots,Ask,slip,Ask-(Stoploss*Point),Ask+(TakeProfit*Point),"",MagicNumber,0,Blue);
// OrderSend(Symbol(),OP_SELL,Lots,Bid,slip,Bid+(Stoploss*Point),Bid-(TakeProfit*Point),"",MagicNumber,0,Red); OrderWatcher=1;

Direction=2;

}

if((myMA*(1-Percent/100))>Ask && Direction!=11 && (Ask<=(LastPrice-(CurrentPipStep*Point))|| myTotal==0)) // Go LONG -> Only buy if >= 30 pips below previous position entry

{

OrderSend(Symbol(),OP_SELL,Lots,Bid,slip,Bid+(Stoploss*Point),Bid-(TakeProfit*Point),"",MagicNumber,0,Red);
// OrderSend(Symbol(),OP_BUY,Lots,Ask,slip,Ask-(Stoploss*Point),Ask+(TakeProfit*Point),"",MagicNumber,0,Blue); OrderWatcher=1;

Direction=1;

}

}

You CANNOT run the firebird EA on anything other than MT4, METATRADER 4. FXCM does not support MT4, so you can't use FXCM.

You can try to go to any broker that has the MT4 platform, for example, interbankfx, and download it from there. Then you have to enable the EA.

--- 帖子 #905 ---
Hi,

I have studied most of the FB code quite intensley. Doing that I stumbled over a bug in the trailing stop code in all known FB EAs (063-TS, 1.0c, 1.0c1).

Since its only a tiny change I try to describe it here:

First, find "TrailingStop" in the code. it should app. look like this:

if(TrailingStop > 0)

{

if((Bid-OrderOpenPrice()) > (Point*TrailingStop))

{

if((OrderStopLoss()) < (Bid-Point*TrailingStop))

{

OrderModify(OrderTicket(),OrderOpenPrice(),Bid-(Point*5),OrderTakeProfit(),0,GreenYellow);

return(0);

}

}

}

}

the bug is the red 5, change it to "TrailingStop" on both places and you are done.

Now the setting of trailingstop does have an effect.

Swissly

--- 帖子 #907 ---
Hi nvwine,

To me this part of the code seems to be a residual from older versions. If you want to get control over all settings directly, you simply look for

SetupGlobalVariables();

quite shortly after start. Insert // at the beginning of the line to gray out the whole line and you are done.

Swissly

--- 帖子 #908 ---

--- 帖子 #909 ---
Swissly,

Both methods work. The reason the 5 pips is used is because when using TrailingStop (t/s) value, the first t/s trigger modifies the new s/l to within 2-3 pips of entry price. If reverse happens now, only 2-3 pips profit. When using 5 pips and t/s=30, the new s/l is set about ~25 pips from entry price. If reverse now, ~25 pips profit.

The advantage of using the t/s, you can have many more t/s modification orders that increments the s/l 2-3 pips more profit each cycle.. This can be beneficial  in long trends. In short trends, which FB likes, you can lose a good part of the +float.

As always, I could be wrong. In my side-by-side forward testing and backtesting the 2 methods, the 5 pips method was substantially more profitable.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #917 ---
Wackena,

Thanks for your explanations, I now see that you had very good reasons for coding like it is;  sorry for calling it a bug!

Is my understanding correct, that you actually didn't implement a classical trailing stop routine but code to catch positions very close (5 pips) to target and lock them in? If this is correct then I have one remark: the variable "TrailingStop" is actually a trailing trigger and not the stop itself. The trigger is a one time shot moving the SL to actual ask-5pips. This also means to me that "TrailingStop" does not come into action if you put it at the level of "TakeProfit", you need to have it some pips below. if for example the TP is 30, TS could be set to 25. This would move the SL to TP-10, as soon as TP-5 is reached.

Swissly

--- 帖子 #929 ---
coolhand,

I added the trailing stop to FB to maximize profits out of trends. For example: t/s=30 is near equivalent to t/p=25. If EA only has t/p, it exits orders at this profit level. But with using t/s, the EA treats t/s as first takeprofit level and if trend continues, additional pips can be made. Using t/s with FB takes nothing away from EA performance, it just increases chance to make additional pips.

Note: As discussed earlier with swissly, If using FBv63g-TS, set t/p above t/s. I suggest setting t/p above expected trends. I use t/p=50. I think setting at 100-150 is a good idea and could allow major pip gains from long reverse trends.

2nd note: For recently started FB EA and how FB handles news events or long trend spikes is determine a lot by when EA was started. Over last 6 weeks, several times I have started same EA on separate Demos, with identical settings, on different days. The results on news event days and strong trends were almost 180 degrees different. For example, one will have sell loses and the other demo will make profits from buys. The longer the Demos run, this effect equalizes out and both perform nearly the same. So judging this EA badly because of short term loses, is not a true evaluation. For me, I critique this EA like I critique my 401K. It is the long haul gains that I want. The last few years, my 401K has seen equity loses of 15-20% during each year. But overall it has gains from year to year. If I can get similar results with FB, I will be happy. Sorry, I'm long winded today.

Wackena

Wackena

--- 帖子 #979 ---
sanchez,

I hope this may help.

1. Put EA in MetraTrader's Experts folder.

2. Open EA with MetaEditor.

3. Confirm correct inputs.

4. Click "Compile" in Menu Bar.

5. Close MetaEditor.

6. Open MetaTrader.

7. Open Currency Pair charts.

8. Open Expert Advisor tab in Navigator window.

9. Click and drag EA to each chart, one at a time.

10. Click Expert Advisor tab in Menu Bar and then you should see Happy Face http://www.forexfactory.com/forexfor...cons/icon7.gif in upper right hand corner of each chart.

11. You are now trading.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #982 ---
My brother had same problem. The dreaded "dong" sound. He was using a satelite dish to receive data and dial-up to send data. This generated a lot of dongs. I'm not sure, but I think the dong sound is result of a Ping failure. The ping is used by broker's server and your MT4 platform to determine good connection. If not, the server or your MT4 generates the dong sound. The FB EA does not have sound code in it. If the excessive loss is triggered, you can get an Alert box with the alert sound.

It can be annoying, but the dongs do not interfer with trading.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #1002 ---
Thoughts & Questions on Firebird<?xml:namespace prefix = o ns = "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:office" /><o></o>
<o></o>

The weeks of Sept 5-15<SUP>th</SUP> have been heartburn weeks for me. Out of my three accounts running Firebird, of course, my live account was the one that took the losses, first two stop losses in GBP, and then I had to manually stop out due to approaching margin call. The first demo account running FB63H2-3, which was started a week earlier and with more funds ($5,000) then my live account (~$3000) had sufficient equity but had floats approaching 50% of equity but survived without any losses and to go on to profit. The 2<SUP>nd</SUP> demo account running FB 1.0b2 was funded with $10,000 and it also approached floats approaching 50% of equity. Unfortunately, my timing was lousy in my live account (running mostly FB63H02-H3, but switched briefly to FB 1.0b2 during the steep trending of the Euro. I had doubled the lot size on the four major pairs I was trading the week before the downtrend in the Euro. This put too much risk into this account resulting in my closing trades when margin calls began to threaten. One thing this did do was to underscore the importance of money management! Instead of sulking too much and becoming depressed I decided to take a look and ask questions and see what I could do to improve the outcome of the EA. I first looked at how the EA works as described in the script noted below:<o></o>

<o></o>
Firebird calculates a 10 day SMA and then shifts it up and down 2% to for a channel. For the calculation of this SMA either close (more trades) or H+L (safer trades) is used.When the price breaks a band a postion in the opposite of the current trend is taken. If the position goes against us we simply open an extra position to average.<o></o>

50% of the trades last a day. 45% 2-6 days 5% longer or just fail.<o></o>

<o></o>

<o></o>

1) Why a 10 day SMA? Why not 15 or 20, etc? What is the advantage of a 10 day SMA?<o></o>

2) Why not automatically close out trades held > 5 days; this would guarantee that most (90-95%) would close in profit, keeping down the float. Those closed out for a loss would be “the cost of doing business” and protect margin.<o></o>

3) In a trending market the V1.0b2, would seem to be more profitable because if the pair trends heavily, the trending side will go to profit while the hedged side will continue to move further away from profit. In a trending market, (how do we determine trending?...maybe by the number of candles in one direction?) the counter-trade should be hedged by less (rather than by an equal amount of the initiated trade.) The hedged part of the trade which should be determined by placing a pending order, should be triggered after the candle closes and determined by the direction or trend of the previous x number of candles. By reducing the amount of the hedge, say by 50%, we have a greater chance of it hitting the profit target. We know that in trending markets the retracements are less than in ranging markets. By limiting the number of days in the market and the amount of the hedge we increase the probability that our target will be hit. The way you could set the hedge percentage amount would be to wait until the initiating candle(s) was formed and then set the hedge amount by a percentage, determined by the strength of the trend…25%, 33%, 50%, 75%, etc., or as has been mentioned in a couple of posts, by fib levels, ie. 23%, 38%, 50%, 68%, 85%... <o></o>

4) If the float is controlled by #3, margin calls are not so much of a problem. <o></o>

5) How does MA Time Frame affect the EA?<o></o>

6) It is absolutely imperative to control the number of open orders. By closing out orders that have not matured in 5 days and/or have gone in the wrong direction by 50% or X% of the stop loss, this allows more profitable trades to be opened up. Trader Seven talks about this in one or two of his posts.<o></o>

7) It is imperative to have money management set up. Human nature is to be greedy, impulsive, etc. A mechanical system based on a set percentage of risk…and I mean total risk…not necessarly risk on each trade is absolutely necessary to survive. If margin approaches a certain percentage, then the EA needs to start closing out the least profitable trades to protect equity! (based on #6.) <o></o>

8) A note about Firebird v. 1.0b2.; the hedging version. When a position goes against you it initiates the pipstep function. Does it enter both a short and a long? Wouldn’t it be preferable to only enter one position, not both positions? If it does enter both positions, this only maximizes possible losses in the wrong direction. It does, however, provide for a profitable trade if the trend continues. Does the pipstep continue to run indefinitely if the position goes against you as more entries are made? If it does, maybe there should be a limit to the number of pipsteps.<o></o>

<o></o>

<o></o>
In looking at my two demo accounts the results are as follows (no losing trades):<o></o>

<o></o>

Version Days Traded Date Total PIPS-PIPs/Day Flt/Eq <o></o>

FB 63H02-03 25 8/14-9/18 4787/191 -3232/+9742 <o></o>
$5000<o></o>

18 Open trades; oldest 9/4; 7>5days<o></o>

<o></o>

FB 1.0b2 19 8/22-9/18 2989/157 -3323/+18010<o></o>
$10,000<o></o>

16 Open trades; oldest 9/1; 7>5 days<o></o>

<o></o>

Conclusions: <o></o>

<o></o>

FB 63H02 gains more PIPS/day but carries twice the float. <o></o>

<o></o>

Comments or thoughts?<o></o>

<o></o>

1Trader2<o></o>

--- 帖子 #1010 ---
Great post!

This particular statement stood out to me because I think it is *very* important.  My live account has been profitable all the way through this difficult time, and float has never exceeded about 25%.  I think the key has been to control the number of open orders.  Personally, I'm using the old V63G and I have no interest in an automated form of control in this area.  I keep tabs on the number of simultaneous open orders, as well as market conditions, and maintain a number that (if they ALL stopped out) would still not result in a margin call.  I believe this is key to the survivability of my trading account... a primary component of successful trading is to "live to fight another day".

This is also my personal opinion, but I think the best way to control the number of open orders is by stopping the EA and allowing existing orders to "flush out" over time.  I've stated this many times, and continue to assert that manually closing trades is a bad idea 99% of the time.  All the testing I have done indicates that arbitrarily closing all open trades once per week (like closing all orders on Friday), or even once per month, has a quite an adverse affect on profits.  Obviously, controlling open orders might not get me the crazy profits we've been seeing in the 80% per month range, but 40% this month is quite acceptable. ;-)

I do have a few "deadbeat" trades hanging around from 2 weeks ago, but they are in the -180 pip range.  Still a far cry from the -300 stoploss.  In keeping with the way this system works, and my results from testing, I plan to leave those trades out there until they close themselves... even if swap eats up the profits.

--- 帖子 #1020 ---
MM can calcuate odd lot sizes like 0.12, 0.23 & etc. Some brokers do not allow odd lot sizes. They need either 0.1 or 0.2 or mini accounts 0.01 type. My NF demo does not allow odd lot sizes. No problem so far with IBFX or FXDD. if your broker does not allow odd lot sizes, then UseMM=false is needed and manually set lot size.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #1024 ---
The purpose of turning off the EA is to control the number of open orders.

I never mentioned anything about "bad trades" in my post.  In my opinion there are no bad trades until they stop out.  They either stop out or limit out.  Although the ones that hang around for awhile can get irritating.  What I don't recommend is closing them before they do one or the other.  Case in point, I'm sure some people besides me had some rather "old" EUR/USD trades hanging around.  Was very tempting to take a 100+ pip hit and dump them 2 days ago, but today was a different story. ;-)

Controlling the # of open orders is what risk management is all about to me.  For my account, the number of open trades is equal to about 60% total account risk.  In other words, if all my open trades stopped out (statistically *very* unlikely, but still pretty aggressive for me), then 40% of my account remains.  Controlling open orders provides me an absolute guarantee that a certain portion of my account is safe at any given time.  Reducing lot size is another method for managing risk, but taken alone it isn't concrete.  No matter what the lot size, potential still exists for enough float to result in a margin call unless there is a cap on the number of open orders.

Obviously, there is a balance between the number of open orders allowed and the lot size for a given account.  We have to allow enough "space" for Firebird to work appropriately, but with guaranteed protection for a portion of our account at the same time.  For me, this is where lot size comes into play.  As I have it sized now, I can have approximately 12 open orders simultaneously across 3 pairs.  This number goes well with my settings, which result in about 3 trades per day.  So far it has worked well even though that is a substantially smaller amount than the floating trades I've seen on some of the statements in this thread.

--- 帖子 #1044 ---
If you're going live, I would use three currency pairs max, on mini-micro trade sizes ($5 margin per lot traded) with $300. So I would load up EUR/USD, USD/CHF, and USD/CAD and set your lot size to ".1" on a mini account like yours. I wouldn't worry about adding another currency pair until you had $500 in account equity. Then at $1,000 I would think about turning up the lots setting to .3 and then to .5 at $2,000. I wouldn't think about going up to full mini-lots until you had at least $3,000 since you're on 200:1 leverage, and that's $50 per full mini lot traded. As well all know, Firebird 1.0C has a habit of running about four trades per pair (in my experience), more or less; so money management is of the utmost importance.

Is big success doable? Most definitely. The trick is the patience and the small steps. You can try and hit the ground running, but I'm not paying your medical bills. That's my bartender's money thank you much...

--- 帖子 #1054 ---
nvwine / wakena -

I just spoke with both IBFX and FXDD.  Here are their policies on getting a margin call.

IBFX's Policy: If Margin level drops below 50%, IBFX will begin randomly closing open positions until Margin level goes above 50%.

FXDD's Policy:  If Margin level drops below 80%, all open positions will be closed.

Now, with regards to fb v1.0c... is there a minmargin level that the ea will not trade below? If not, can that be included in the code?

--- 帖子 #1060 ---
dscott5912,

I got your PM.

In v1.0c, you need to monitor Margin Level % manually to avoid margin calls from broker.

In v1.0c1, the EA auto-monitors Margin Level %. will stop opeing new trades if margin level % falls below the Input MinMarginLevel setting. This does not eliminate the danger. If MinMarginLevel is set too close to Broker's margin call level (ie; FDXX 80%), then existing orders that increase in negative float, can still initiate the margin call. This is why, my MinMarginLevel setting is 250.

v1.0c1 should work OK on standard and mini accounts to control margin level %.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #1070 ---
Hi Rusty,

A trending market will kill any firebird. The beauty of those three pairs is that even though they do trend, they don't hang around at the extremes as much as others, like the GBPUSD, do. They tend to return to the median, which is where your firebird will pick up pips.

Right now I'm running two demo accounts. One is running 63G TS, the other 63G.

63G TS is trading USDCHF, USDCAD, and EURUSD on a 5M timeframe. It has net profit of $1200, including a $700 floating loss. No losers, running for about two weeks.

63G is trading USDCHF, USDCAD, EURUSD, GBPUSD, and USDJPY, on a 1M timeframe. It has net profit of about $1200, including a $800 floating loss. 4 losers, all GBPUSD, again running for about 2 weeks.

Back to your question, I'd run firebird 63G TS on a 5M chart, with USDCAD, USDCHF, and EURUSD.

Remember, always think safety first. You want to stay in the game, and the while the GBPUSD can give you a lot of pips, it also has a very healthy appetite for firebirds! Chews them up and spits them out.

Just my 2.

regards,

Horace, you nailed it! You cannot just start this ea and expect it to make you money without some management, such as turning it off during news announcements, or what I do is turn it off when I'm not trading, such as overnight. My experience is closing orders in the black now is better than hoping the ea will close them later in profit. That's one reason I like the trailing stop more than the fixed tp. I'm still researching accrete's idea of creating an ea that will determine market conditions and start the appropriate ea to meet those conditions. I leave my live account on at all times.  That is why I call it automatic trading.

I just let it rip live with smallish lots at first, until I get an idea how it really works.  All my demos are run through all news events also, so I already had some idea of what to expect.

--- 帖子 #1093 ---
For me it's just a calculation of risk based on the stop loss assigned to each trade.

I never allow total risk from all open orders to exceed 60% of my account. Knowing that FB is a "counter trend" system, I know I have to allow it the opportunity to pile up a fair number of trades. With that in mind, I have to tailor my lot sizes accordingly. Right now I have my lots sized to allow for about 10 open orders, and I'm currently using 2 pairs (EUR/USD & USD/CAD). I don't interfere with # of orders per pair or anything, just total open orders... and I don't cut profits by closing trades early. ;-) As of this moment, my balance is up 82% and equity has never exceeded 20% since going live on 8/17, so I'm not in a hurry to make any changes.

To me it seems the prime difficulty with FB is protecting profits. We've seen a lot of gold fever on this and the other thread and people have allowed FB to trade their accounts into oblivion without even encountering a stop loss. All in pursuit of 100% (month on month) rates of return. Personally, I think even the 50% I got last month is stupid high and it scares me a little. So probably even 60% total account risk is unwise, but I'm greedy too... ;-)

Just my two cents and certainly not scientific in my analysis!
