NOt sure about all your questions but here goes:

Use the FB v1.0a available in the first post of this thread.

On a thousand dollar mini lot I would trade four pairs at .25 mini lots. I am using the USDCHF, EURUSD, USDJPY, and USDCAD to good effect.

Use the M5 charts.  I think 25-250-25 is good.  Percent setting is 0.1.

When (we hope) your account grows to $2000 in equity simply change the lots traded to .5 minilots per pair.  I use the old rule of  1 minilot per pair per $1000 in account  equity.  (That would be .1 lot  on a standard account).

Be mentally prepared for a drawdown at first. Mine sure did!  About 20%. But for the first full month of live trading I have now netted 1060 pips.

Obviously you will not be rich by next year on this method but your risk of margin calls should be minimal I would think.

Good luck.

--- 帖子 #1162 ---
Fellow Firebird'ers -

This version includes the added level of protection of MinMarginLevel. I feel this is important especially for those of us that don't have much to open with.

MinMarginLevel is good because you can set it to not open any trades once it hits a certain percentage. Why is this important? If your account falls below a certain percentage, your broker will either close all your positions or randomly close positions just to get you back over the margin level they decide. Margin level was new to me coming from RefcoFX and FXCM because they went strictly by available margin (or Free Margin). If you ran out of margin, you got an instant margin call liquidating all your open positions.

Each broker has a different policy and you'll need to contact them. I have already spoken personally with both FXDD and IBFX. Here are their policies:FXDD:  If margin level falls below 80%, all open positions will be closed

IBFX:  If margin level falls below 50%, they will randomly start closing positions until your margin level goes above 50%.
When I first started to demo fb v1.0, I noticed way too many positions were being opened for the amount of margin I had and knew I wouldn't be comfortable with seeing that on a live account.

The first step was turning on money management using microlots (IBFX) since I was opening with $350. I also had to make one small change in the UseMM math to make sure I was getting 30 cents a pip for 3 micro lots vs .03 cents a pip. ;-)

The other step was implementing MinMarginLevel. I found fb v1.0c1 out on forex-tsd included MinMarginLevel for MAtype 0, but not for type 1. I have included it for type 1 as well. It works for both MA types now.

MinMarginLevel and Money management should be 2 key ingredients with any EA.

Since v1.0a didn't include money management or margin level protection, I have taken the liberty of including both in v1.0a.

One additional note under UseMM (money management):

The original code uses Lots=AccountEquity()* Risk/100/1000;

In order to make this work properly with IBFX and miniaccounts, I changed it to Lots=AccountEquity()* Risk/100/100;

If you are using FXDD, you'll want to change it back to Lots=AccountEquity()* Risk/100/1000;

I have found this helpful in protecting myself, I hope others find it useful as well.

From what I have read in most of the FB Documentation, FB was supposed to average the TP level of the pipstep orders. So that the trend FB was stuck in would only have to come back a portion of the way to break even. All  the pipstep orders I have seen leave the original orders as-is. I am not sure if the bug has been fixed (check the last few lines of the EA code). Am I right in this??  Fixing this might help with large drawdowns, and old trades effecting our margins.

--- 帖子 #1183 ---
Well, just fyi. If you trade .03 lots when opening a mini demo, you'll actually be getting .03 cents a pip (on EUR/USD). With money management turned on, your fb ea should trade 0.40 lots or sometimes 0.30 lots which equates to .40 cents or .30 cents which is safe in my book. Also be aware that the default for risk is 10%. If you want your risk to be less than 10%, you'll need to modify that in the user settings which you can do when you first load the EA... or you can do after the fact by pressing F7.

--- 帖子 #1184 ---
Because some brokers, including IBFX, use the suffix "m" on Mini Accounts charts, all Firebird Fixed versions probably will not place order on jpy pairs.

The code on all Fixed versions should have this modification. These include versions v1.0a, v1,0b(1,2,3), v1.0c(1).

Existing code:

Inserted Code
if ((Symbol()=="EURJPY") || // FIXED BY SKYLINE ON 11 Aug 2006
(Symbol()=="USDJPY") ||
(Symbol()=="CHFJPY") ||
(Symbol()=="AUDJPY") ||
(Symbol()=="CADJPY") ||
(Symbol()=="NZDJPY") ||
(Symbol()=="GBPJPY") ||
(Symbol()=="SGDJPY"))

Change above code to:

Inserted Code
if ((Symbol()=="EURJPY") || (Symbol()=="EURJPYm") || // FIXED BY SKYLINE ON 11 Aug 2006
(Symbol()=="USDJPY") || (Symbol()=="USDJPYm") ||
(Symbol()=="CHFJPY") || (Symbol()=="CHFJPYm") ||
(Symbol()=="AUDJPY") || (Symbol()=="AUDJPYm") ||
(Symbol()=="CADJPY") || (Symbol()=="CADJPYm") ||
(Symbol()=="NZDJPY") || (Symbol()=="NZDJPYm") ||
(Symbol()=="GBPJPY") || (Symbol()=="GBPJPYm") ||
(Symbol()=="SGDJPY") || (Symbol()=="SGDJPYm"))

Wackena

Code modified for standard lots:

//----------------------- USER INPUT

extern int MA_length = 10;

extern int MA_timeframe = 15;

extern int MAtype = 0; //0=close, 1=HL

extern double Percent = 0.05;

extern int TradeOnFriday = 1;

extern int slip = 100; //exits only

extern bool UseMM = 0; // Money Management - 1 = true & 0 = false

extern double Risk = 1.0; // percent of account equity to risk per trade

extern double Lots = 1.0; // modified by MoneyMa$ter

extern int TakeProfit = 50;

extern int Stoploss = 100; // total loss on all open positions in pips // modified by Renato

extern double TrailingStop = 10; // modified by MoneyMa$ter
// Ron added for iFXAnalyzer

extern int Fast_Period = 23;

extern int Fast_Price = PRICE_OPEN;

extern int Slow_Period = 84;

extern int Slow_Price = PRICE_OPEN;

extern double DivergenceLimit= 0.002;

extern bool Use_V63D_Divergence = 1; // 0 - Use original method for divergence, 1 - use in iFXAnalyzer
extern int PipStep = 40;//if position goes this amount of pips against you add another.

extern double IncreasementType = 0;//0=just add every PipStep, >0 =OrdersToal()^x *Pipstep
double Stopper=0;

double KeepStopLoss=0;

double KeepAverage;

double dummy;

double spread=0;

double CurrentPipStep;

int OrderWatcher=0;
// Ron Adds

int maxDD=0;

int maxOO=2;

--- 帖子 #1188 ---
that is the TS doing that, looking at your setting above, your TS is 10, such that, when the price moves 10pips in profit your SL gets reassigned to breakeven, as it moves more into profit the the SL keeps getting moved up and up with it, so eventually if there is a reversal, it will hit the newly defined SL which is actually in profit thanks to the TS.

--- 帖子 #1191 ---
MoneyMa$ter,

t/s has a catch 22. The good point is that it can secure profits if price does not quite reach t/p. It does this just as you described above. The catch 22 is that after s/l is set by t/s, then price reverses a little before proceeding. the s/l can be trigger by the reverse and then potential t/p profit is not gained. With FB type EAs, I've found the s/l to be beneficial as many times price will reverse strongly before reaching t/p. Without t/s and s/l of 300, orders can stay open a long time. Using t/s closes many orders so new order can be opened.

Just my opinion.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #1200 ---
Percent controls the quantity of trades because it relates to price action outside the band created by FireBird: further from the band, fewer trades. Quality is a function of the other settings, such as lotsize, TF, TP, TS and SL. Getting the settings right is akin to determining the combination to a vault - once all the chambers align the door opens and the vault yields its riches.

So to answer your question, I think I've found a high percentage of quality trades because I've tinkered with settings, finding a great combination for standard lots. Fully sixty percent of my losses were "NFP induced"; another 20% or so were due to a tight SL of 42 which doesn't work for me. Eliminating the "NFP induced" losses and changing the SL significantly improved the trade quality.

Highly volatile pairs I think should be traded on 5 min (or higher??) charts. That's explained in the thread somewhere and I think it's true. Some traders stay away from the volatile pairs (that's probably the longest timeframe ).

--- 帖子 #1202 ---
When you get a new demo each month with IBFX the history is gone. On a live account or a demo that does not expire all history should be there.

With the terminal window open select the 'account history' tab right mouse click over the trades in history and select 'all history' from the mouse pop-up menu. You should see all history including deposits. If you do not I would complain loud and long to the broker on a live account. When you right click there are other periods you can select including custom periods. When ever we start a new month my live accounts, by default, only show the current month until I right click and select a longer history period. It somtimes takes several seconds after you select 'all history' to display properly if you have had the account for a long time.

--- 帖子 #1211 ---
For those of you interested in using money management and/or margin level protection with v63H03, I have included it.

You have the option of turning either one off or on when you first load it (or afterwards by pressing F7) on the "Inputs" tab. One cautionary note under money management. If you are using a miniaccount with IBFX, the formula coded in the UseMM routine will work correctly. If you are using a miniaccount with another broker, like FXDD, you will need to change the following code from ...

Lots=AccountEquity()* Risk/100/100;  // specific for minilots with IBFX

to ...

Lots=AccountEquity()* Risk/100/1000;  // other broker like FXDD

IBFX calculates this a bit different on a mini is why.

*** As always, please be sure to test any modified EA before going live ***

--- 帖子 #1230 ---
As others have stated, lowering the percentage generates more orders. This mainly applies to 1st order on chart. After 1st order, remaining multiple chart orders only trigger when price reaches PipStep setting. So, even if Envelope and RVI triggers are made, the order will not be placed until PipStep is reached.

Wackena

Traderone,

My apologies for the late response. Just getting to a binary-based, table-top accessory (aka laptop); buying crude all evening! Russian D2 to be exact. But I digress.

I was demo-trading 12 currency pairs on a standard lot so float got relatively high, like $2000-$3000. But that also included FLYER! test lots. Yes there were still open pairs trading that I manually closed. Trading universe now reduced to 8 (fib?) with a goal of 6 pairs for live trading.

I've contributed (don't like the "L" word) as high as $16,000 in a single trade (live) so I'm not really concerned about 100 pips. I think it can be avoided however. Those losses seemed to occur because the trade opened by FB never moved into profit which, had the trade moved far enough in profit, would have allowed a revision of the SL to BE. Major losses (100 pips in my test-cases) happened because the trade opened and went straight south (or north) to the SL. I had numerous trades close in profit because FB moved SL to BE. Didn't make TP but made a profit. And that's the name of the game. Profit.

Possible solution: if trade never moved into profit, or if entry price is never exceeded and current price hits a predetermined point defined by trader, like negative 65 pips for example (or less) from the entry, then program FB to liquidate the trade. Differs from a pure SL because in my scenario if prices did initially move toward profit, then there's a chance the trend will reverse and become profitable again. But when prices immediately move to loss territory, it seems to continue all the way unabated to SL. I'd like to liquidate before the full SL is hit.

Programmable?

--- 帖子 #1250 ---
FB-TS and fixed versions has sub-routines that are not used, CloseTheseTrades() and CloseLoosingTrades() .

CloseTheseTrades() will just close all trades. I believe this was intended to be used in an end of week or bad trading time routine to close all orders.

CloseLoosingTrades() uses a Trend indicator based on H4 timeframe to exit orders when a strong trend is detected. This sub-routine could be modified to close orders that have been open for X amount of time and has X amount of loss. I'm not aware as to how to track if order was in profit at one time, but at some later time it is in loss. I could only code EA to trigger an action on conditions at one period of time.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #1269 ---
Attached is Firebird-v2.0. This is standard Firebird with the following.

1. Money Management (UseMM) to use % (Risk) of account equity to set lot size.

2. Trailing Stop.

3. Maximum number of open orders per chart (MaxOpenOrders).

4. Minimum Margin Level (MinMarginLevel) to stop trading.

5. CloseLoosingTrades = true;.

Requires a and b.

a. Input CloseHour. Number of hours elapsed since order was opened.

b. Input LossLevel. Amount of Loss.

This EA has fix to trade JPY pairs on standard and IBFX Mini accounts.

Wackena

Download EA from Post http://www.forexfactory.com/forexfor...postcount=1277

--- 帖子 #1282 ---
Allow me one point:

(1) It's possible that YOU could discover something new. Use anything; play around with it and vary the timeframes. That's why we call it "testing on a demo account".

Now to your question:

FB 2 is the original FB, plus the addition of MoneyManagement and Trailing Stop, plus correction for the yen pairs, plus the new features Wackena just added. So whatever timeframe you used successfully in the past can still be used in the future.

Works like this:

(1) Shorter TFs result in more trades;

(2) Longer TFs result in fewer trades.

(3) Conversely, smaller Percents, more trades and higher percents, fewer trades.

(4) Some traders use TF of 1 minute, others use 5 minutes, others use higher TFs like 30 for the more volatile pairs such as cable; still others avoid cable altogether.

(5) For standard lots, I'm testing with 5m charts a 1m charts produced quite a few trades and a correspondingly high float.  Definitely avoiding cable.

Cheery-o. Good hunting and all that sort of rot.

--- 帖子 #1286 ---
hi all,

Look, i hate to be a damp squib for you lot on here using this, but i felt I had to give out a warning and maybe open some eyes.

why? well i can see the same situation arising that happened a few weeks ago - everything swimming along nicely, everyone demo testing and making loadsa pips - gaining confidence, feeling invincible.  The went on for about 6 weeks or more.

just as everone started opening live accounts the market went trendy and lots lost a bundle.

Now the reason i'm saying this is that thereare a lot of new faces on here and i don't want you to get burned.

Now, for opening your eyes. - some will remain blinkered

The reason you like this strategy and the reason it is so popular is this.

You never have to take a loss. - thats why newbies and unseasoned traders flock to this like a moth to a flame.

But it's not real.  You do take a loss ..... eventually.  and its a total loss.

what happens is that as you are watching this you see lots of green on your account balance page so you feel invincible. - even seeing some people take 100 pip losers has no impact because you are making hundreds more right?

well, ignore that page and concentrate on what has become known as 'the float'

The account equity is the most important figure to watch when you are using firebird. - it's here that you will see your drawdown - how many of you would really play a strategy if someone said to you - you will have to put up with a 50% drawdown though"

well thats exactly what happens with firebird - watch that float figure because that is your indcation of drawdown. and one day, it wont stop.

Don't get me wrong, this is certainly intruiging and as a trader it's really interested me following your progress over the past few months.

But i have to tell you it is fools gold and is not tradable.

The second reason it seems attractive is that it appears to make hundreds of pips a week or day.  The thing is that because you cannot play it at the same staking level as other strategies is that you have to account for this.

For example.  lets say that you have a strategy that makes 200 pips a month on a single pair - pretty low you may think but thats your inexperience speaking.

However this 200 pips you can comfortably play at $10 a pip on a $10k account (thats 10:1 leverage).

with firebird lets say that you are only comfortable enough to play it at $1 a pip because of the 'float' as you call it - drawdown as i call it

well, that means that it has to make 2000 pips a month to give the same monetary result as to 200 pip strategy - see what i mean?

If you could comfortably play firebird at $10 a pip on one pair then i'd say it was great - even if it will bite your bum eventually.  But because you can only play it at flat (ie zero) leverage then i would plump for the 200 pip strategy every time.

Now i know some have been on here saying that you should play $1 for every $1k in your account - but believe me, you will soon die if you do that.

So, just a word of warning and dont come running to me when it happens.

--- 帖子 #1287 ---
Two Points:

(1) Count it quite simply as the cost of doing business. As an entrepreneur, I understand and accept the costs and risks involved. For example, while SL 300 may work for micros and minis, I think SL 300 is an inappropriate risk for trading standard lots. So the obvious thing to do is reduce the SL for standard lot trading.

(2) Understand there are many well-educated, experienced and creative traders at FF more than capable of first, identifying then second, overcoming FB's shortcomings. Consider the following example. Original FB could trend until it hit your SL; at 300 that could be a pretty good hit. Wackena modified the program to reduce such losses.

It's rather naive to think you'll operate any nascent business without a loss. And an EA less than a year old is akin to a new business. The question cabletrader is how much loss is acceptable and how do you minimize those losses. Furthermore, none of us think this or any EA will always and forever operate perfectly without observation and modification, fine tuning so to speak, in order to derive maximum efficient operation.

Don't ever give up; don't ever quit. Quitting is the easy way out and for some, quitting is simply not an option. Rather use your mind and contribute constructive criticism that will improve the project. That means highlight the shortcomings, then recommend a solution.

Adapt, improvise and dominate.

--- 帖子 #1289 ---
This morning, as of 11:15 am est, FB closed 15 trades, all in profit, total of 154 pips, standard lots, using 5 minute charts, no cable. Current float approx -$900. Maybe I'll try 1M.

IMHCO, ("C" is for conservative) a system generating $1,500 - $3,000 profit per day, against $900 - $1,200 in negative float is a winning system. Truth is you realize profit daily, while the negative float doesn't offset profits unless and until the trader decides to close those open trades at the end of the week or prior to a major announcement such as NFP. So conservatively speaking, 4 days at an average of $2,000/day is $8,000, less the closing day negative float of let's say $1,500, leaves a net of $6,500 for a week's work or around 25 large per month.

Slow compared to newstrading but steady. And the name of the game is "profit"!!! Like I said last week, it's the fully loaded FB (MM, TS, Close Losers, Close open too long, Yen corrected), a virtual pip mobile, unstoppable, low on gas and environmentally friendly!

To Fellow Firebirders,

Yes, your account can "blow Up." My live account went from a modest $2800 to $5600 in about 5 weeks. I thought FB & I were invincible and I couldn't lose. I began over risking and trading too many pairs. And of course at the worst possible time when I doubled all of my lot sizes, the summer ranging ended and the trend began. The float quickly ate me up, and I manually had to close trades to prevent a margin call with all trades closing. It took me all the way down to $1200 in about 4 days.

I continue to believe in Firebird, but I have a new respect for it and have a better understanding of it.  I will be "wiser" next time.

I think it behooves all of us to respect the market. It has a life of its own. The market is the "shark" and we are the "prey." We have to learn to swim faster and smarter so that we can become bigger and survive within it. God wants us to succeed in life, but He has lessons for each of us to learn. Sometimes God humbles us through our pain (whether it be through loss of money, fortune or fame). One's life can change in an instant (through illness, death of a loved one or our own.) Remember, that God owns everthing including the money He has entrusted to you to use for your benefit (or if you choose your demise) and your family's. I have lost a lot of money in the markets (options, stocks, Forex), probably money I may never recover. But it has taught me lessons...a tuition of sorts if you may. Tread the markets with caution, tend toward the conservative side, think outside the box, recognize an opportunity when it arises, and on and on. Just a little philosophy for the day...

1Trader2

--- 帖子 #1320 ---
Reviewed the code.

The condition under which FB liquidates a losing trade is an "and" not an "or" gate. I thought it was an "or" gate in this instance.

In other words, if a trade has been open for "x" hours [like 36] AND pips lost exceeds or equals the designated "liquidate-point-because-of-the-number-of-pips-lost", then FB liquidates the position. Both the "x" hours and "number of pips lost" are trader-provided. The idea is to cut your losses and prevent FB from continuing to the designated SL which at 300 for micros and 100 for standards can be a decent hit. In my tests, that's been the most significant and latest (and last?) obstacle to results without spot or blemish.

--- 帖子 #1332 ---
Thom,

Yes, weekend hours are included.

The CloseLoosingTrades works on Server time. In your example above: I use IBFX and server time is GMT-4. Order opened Thursday 00:00 GMT = 20:00 my server time. CloseHour=72, LossLevel=100. if OrderProfit() is below $ -100, then, if PC is running, order should close Sunday after 20:00 server time.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #1337 ---
Thanks Chad,

You've brought into sharp relief two of the several major philosophical points of Firebird as set forth below:

(1) For those of you trading micros on FB, -1,500 pips should be something you can patiently wait out for days like Chad successfully did; SL 300 is easy.

But

(2) For those of you interested in trading standard lots, -1,500 pips can approximate $15,000 (for just 1 lot, forgetting multiple currencies and forgetting about margin requirements for now). For some, that's a lotta cheddar, jack. So SL is reduced to perhaps 100 (or less), with the 36 hour plus 65-pips-down-cut-your-losses option (although that didn't help today because the trends moved 100 pips in less than 24 hours; gotta stop that unabated run to SL somehow).

Both approaches are legitimate trading strategies, investments requiring not only your time and money but also your emotional energy.

Always understanding there's a degree of risk as my friend TraderOne pointed out, always accepting responsibility for the risk you incur for the hopefully commensurate, profit, the question simply boils down to: "How much (pressure, stress, nail-biting, stomach-churning, gut-wrenching, teeth-clenching, sleepless nights, worrying, grayhair,) for YOU is too much?"

Remember, when the pressure comes, it will squeeze out whatever's deep inside of you.

Just information; not a recommendation.

--- 帖子 #1347 ---
let say your trailingstop set to 30,

once your positions is +30 pips

then, your stop loss will move to currentbid-5pips for buy order, and currentask+5 pips ' for sell order.

in wackena's firebird trailingstop code, after stoploss moved once, it will not move any further even your position is +80pips, or +120pips.

i wished there's someone who can code the latter part of trailingstop, like in the next +30 pips, stoploss will move again.

Chad

Life goes on

--- 帖子 #1348 ---
I'm not too sure about that Chad. The way the TS has worked for me is in this sence, say my TS is 10pips, upon hitting 10pips, the TS moves my SL to breakeven, then every other equal move, it will again adjust the SL pip by pip, which is why i can close out in some positions with anywhere from 1-49 pips, even though my TP is 50, because the TS moved my SL to that point.

Hi there, i am running 3 MT4 IBFX demo (GMT on server) accounts as follows on 5m charts:

FB 63H04 defaults time to trade 0/24 on UsdChf, UsdCad, EurUsd, EurChf

FB 63H04-TS defaults time to trade 0/24 on UsdChf, UsdCad, EurUsd, EurChf

FBv2 defaults (except close loosing trades set to false**) time to trade 6/16 on UsdChf, UsdCad, EurUsd, EurChf

**A note on the FBv2 "close loosing trades" setting. I noticed (and asked the Q last week) that if there are loosing trades going into the weekend if the setting would include the non-trading-hours of the weekend in it's calculations. Yes it will. So last Friday, with three loosing trades at -60ish or greater average, i decided to turn this feature to false in my default setting as i wanted to give the trades at leaset a day or two in the new week to see if they would recover. They did so in today's (Monday) trading session. All three closed out in profit. The CAD had S/L kick in and closed at +11, E/U TP hit at +25, CHF TP hit at +25. This was a case when closing out the trades would have taken a big hit on the account. Though i realize the market could have also continued against the EA's entries. Just typing that last sentence out is an interesting thought. I used to blame everything on my Mamma wearing combat boots, or the sun in my eyes...grin.

--- 帖子 #1386 ---
Hey All:

I have to say, Firebird is a great EA to have in your portfolio for ranging markets. I just shut down and cashed out all open trades. I've been running live 24x7 since Oct 2nd. Overall, profitable.

Just my opinion, but the swings seem to to be getting a little to wide. I was down over 27% in floating loss at one point. Mono's 30/300/30 kept me in the game (Thanks Man!).

My own 2 cents:

1) Pick currencies that are going to range

2) Position your lots accordingly. 300 pip swings with ~10 open trades will put the squeeze on your confidence

3) Interest will kill you if trades sit for too long. (Almost 40% of my profits went to pay the man)

4) Shorter up/down cycles are where this baby shines.

Used v63h02 on USDCAD, EURUSD, USDCHF 30/300/30

Started v1.0c on the 12th for NZDUSD

Anybody have any ideas how to use this baby long term? I'm afraid a long term trend is about to hit the $.

berdj

I run Firebird V63G-TS

traderlismiss

I belive it has to do with the steppip setting. I have mine on 40 as you see it makes a few trades therefore not putting my account at risk.

the point of the pipstep is to open a new position every time the pair move from the last open position.therefore if you have it at 10 it will open a new position every time the pair move 10 pips away from the last position it opened.

Therefore if the pair moved 50 pips you are going to have 4 trades.thats ok if your margin can take it.

And if your running 6 pairs well you could have at less 24 new trades .

Also I run my charts on 5 min TF.do not change the TF in the ea leave it at 15min.

A very good friend of mine back tested them for me and we found that the 5min TF gave the best returns.

And again I trade the GBP/USD...I know some of you dont but as you can see from the statement it returns the most.

I hope I am able to help in some way..

Glenn

--- 帖子 #1486 ---
I am running live FB v2, which is doing ok...........

Here is my dilemma, (please see attached file) i had a sell order open for eur/usd at 15:15 11/09 GMT at 1.2805, T/P was established at 1.2790.

Well please have a look at the file, because it shows my T/P price reached, but order never closed. Has anyone seen this before, please let me know?

--- 帖子 #1487 ---
That's because the exit price is the ask (bid+spread) price not the bid.  if you have a 2 pip spread then the exit price will actually be 1.2788 (bid) which is 1.2790 ask.  The chart is showing the bid price or depending on the broker it could show the average of the 2.  So it needs to go 2 pips lower to close the trade.

Hope that makes sense.

Wiz.

--- 帖子 #1495 ---
FireBird v.2 Results for the Week

Trading live on 5 minute charts, with standard lots, 13 winners no losers, currently no negative float (all trades closed for weekend), 136 pips profit. This was a conservative trading week in that:

(1) I disabled pipstep-driven increases and allowed trading one lot per currency pair at any given time;

(2) I traded for only three days and five currency pairs (pls see my earlier post and report); and

(3) Some trades were manually closed.

My settings for standard lots are:

extern int MA_length = 10;

extern int MA_timeframe = 15;

extern int MAtype = 0;

extern double Percent = 0.05;

extern int TradeOnFriday = 1;

extern int slip = 100;

extern bool UseMM = 0;

extern double Risk = 5;

extern double Lots = 1.0;

extern int TakeProfit = 20;

extern int Stoploss = 150;

extern double TrailingStop = 10;

extern int MaxOpenOrders = 1;

extern double MinMarginLevel = 250;

extern bool CloseLoosingTrades = true;

extern int CloseHour = 36;

extern int LossLevel = 80;

WARNING:

Please note that based on these settings for standard lots, the worse case scenario is a $1,500 adverse move should any one currency pair move against your position by 150 pips within less than 36 hours!!!! That didn't happen to me this week but you should know the potential exists.

I did see some pretty large negative floats. For example, cable alone at one time was -$300 plus, while total float was -$1,800 and more. I got on an airplane, left the trades open and eventually each negative position reversed to profit.

Point is, if you don't have the stomach, personality trait and capital for this type of trading, my advice is that you stick with micro and mini accounts.

I have been testing FB for about 8 months.  Went through a period in August and pretty much blew out a real account.  I have been experimenting with different methods of money management, closing trades manually earlier, etc. I've tried being more conservative entering trades also.  I've decided to revisit my thinking somewhat and let the EA do most of the work.  I believe that the key is money management.  My most recent experiment started at the beginning of this week.  I took my trades from the past 8 months and analyzed them.  The data pretty much agreed with Trader 7 statement in the beginning of the EA:  50% of the trades last a day. 45% 2-6 days 5% longer or just fail.  So the way I figured it was to close all trades that have gone longer than 120 hours.  My data shows that the majority of those that go to the SL of 200-300 pips are those that go longer than 5 days.  I am using FB 63HO4_TS_MM.  I have a close trades feature in it that closes the trades after x hours.  I believe that this was added to version 2.0.  I just pasted it into this version as I believe it (63H04) is the most profitable version.  My object is to open a fair amount of trades using the Major 4.  I have set the envelope % to 0.05, pipstep to 30 and TP & SL to settings in version 1.0c as set up by Mono.  It is posted in the first post of this thread.  My theory is that if FB runs into a trend that the losing trades will exit earlier before hitting their full SL, and that the float will be lower because the trades open will only be 5 days old.  We will see.  I will post my results over the next couple months.

1 Trader2

--- 帖子 #1499 ---
Glenn,

Thanks for taking the time to give some thought to my setup. Let me say I agree with you....I'm just taking a conservative approach as described below.

TS 10 can take me out at every little retracement and sometimes it prevents moving to the full TP, but it also produces a profit (albeit small at 7-8 pips). I believe pigs get fat...hogs get slaughtered. My little piggy approach is conservative and though the trade closes, it closes at a profit. FireBird can open another trade for that pair at the appropriate time.

During demo testing I had set TP at 18 (not a Fib number). Why? Because I noticed currencies seemed to often move to 18 pips profit, then reversed considerably to the down side creating a terribly high negative float. That's cool for demo testing and mini accounts but remember I'm trading standard lots live. So it made sense to me to take the smaller profit, close the trade and live to fight another day with a new trade. If anything, I may revert to TP 18.

As to the SL 150, that was increased from 55 I think it was, because 55 was too close, came too quick and didn't allow room to breathe. That's getting stopped out at $550. I'm definitely not going to SL 300 for standard lots!

Also, if a trade is losing 80 or more pips for 36 hours, FireBird will liquidate the position. I don't know if anyone else tested or traded standard lots so I was seeking a number acceptable to me and for now its SL 150. Could reduce it to the 100-125 range. Mathematically, there's a SL for standard lots that's the equivalent of SL300 successfully used for mini/micro trading and it seems to be in the 85-150 range. But it's really not a factor, unless the market enters a trend in which case I would manually halt trading.

The risk/reward ratio bothers me not. I don't know how to spell "risk averse"! I'm either: (a) taking profit at 20 or (b) the trailing stop kicks in for the smaller profit. So I'm in and out at profit, maybe not for 50 pips but it's steady and consistent. This week I made 136 pips trading basically something less than three days? Doesn't pay for AvGas or JP-3 but I can live with those 136 pips. Remember...pigs get fat...hogs get slaughtered! I will continue tweaking the setup.  Further, when I'm more comfortable, I can then increase the program to multiple lots with its higher margin requirements, higher negative float and most importantly the corresponding profit increase!

--- 帖子 #1509 ---
The function is called, but does nothing for the TP because FB passes the "false" to the function as

ChangeOpenOrders(false, myTotal, AveragePrice);

As a result, it does not modify the TP. I have done a test to pass the "true", all positions can be modified for their TP to the same level. Good or not? When the TP is hit, all positions will be closed. Mostly, it needs to wait long time, sometimes, it just misses some good chance.

Thanks!

my setting are based on a slow growth, thats why  my pipstep is set in the range 35-40.....

yes my settings and pairs have been changing, I run several pairs on a demo account at the same time with the same settings as my live account therefore i am able to review at the end of a week/month the returns per pair.

based on that information I change the pair mix the next week on my live account. however at the moment I belive I have the ideal three pairs and I have no intention of changing them.

I only run three pair because of the possible negative float ( mine has been max at $657.00).

In the early stages back testing was done mainly with the view to find ideal time frames.

I prefer to forward test and run it on a demo has I believe backtesting will only tell you so much...and you cant beat live/demo trading.

Because I now feel very comfortable with my setup any changes from now on will only be minor...fine tuning....to gain maximum returns per pair.

Just my 2 cents. I have 2 firebird demo accounts and both are doing very well. I posted the results from one earlier today and we'll say that is my 1st account. My second account has been running for a few more days and has Skyline's settings of 30-300-30. This account while generating a bit more profit has a much higher float. With glenn5t's settings I have about a 10% of profit float, while the skyline settings have about a 30% of profit float. Bottom line is, neither account has had a single loss. Both accounts have a good profit. So i guess my point is, if you are not worried about the margin you could use skyline's settings and have just a bit more profit. If however like most of us you are concerned about the float, I suggest glenn5t's settings. With the small float that I have in account 1, I am thinking about trading an additional pair. Not endorcing anything, just my 2 cents.

Hi Daniel

I have only been here a short time compaired to others, but Welcome to Forex Factory, and the Firebird thread.

Just a couple of things, give your self about 2-3 hours or so and read this thread, and this one, http://www.forexfactory.com/forexfor...ead.php?t=5012 from page one to the current post. There is SO much info, that no one could put it into one post. I am not saying this to be mean, but to help you. FB won't make you rich overnight, but it can make you poor really quick, so 2 hours or so is a small price to pay, and it will answer most of your questions you have, and many you didn't think you had. It has helped me more then i can explain. You will learn what works, and what doesn't, and why. In the 2 threads there is the original PDF document that explains how it works, or should work. You will find probably no less then 6 different versions of FB each suited to a different way of thinking, a few web pages with more resources, maybe 50 or so reports from different users showing the results they have had with FB, etc... There really is no other way to learn how to use this Script. If you want to start out on a demo, which you really should, you can find the version I am using on page 95 of this thread, using the settings from Glenn5t. His settings can be found around page 92 of this thread, I think. Good luck, we are all here to help

Rusty

--- 帖子 #1586 ---
I'm not a very active poster here, but I have experimented with FB for quite a while now. Doing that I also analyzed the code in detail to understand its function. From there I can say that changing timeframes from 1M unto 30M does only change one thing: Initially done for backtesting, FB supresses new orders for the time of 2 bars after a trade has happend (open or close). This means that FB's running pure without TS should see smaller differences, if TS is used then differences could be substantial. Imagine a situation where price is above the channel and a order gets closed by TS, then with 1M a next trade could be opened after 2 minutes, with 30M only after 1h.

Happy trading

Swissly

--- 帖子 #1587 ---
I've only become engaged in this thread over the last several days (with many hours spent reading/researching). I've been keeping track of different people's settings along with changes that they've made. I'll probably post some kind of summary post soon as I'm about to deploy a number of demo tests based on settings from some of the more successful installations to date.

The problem (or maybe the beauty, depending upon your perspective) with these long threads is that they meander and at times it's very difficult to piece together exactly what others are doing.

These threads operate best when the first post points to an actively managed Web page which includes the following: FAQ, links to popular settings/versions/docs and/or key posts. Anything less than this leads to lots of folks wandering around asking the same questions over and over. (Hey, sort of like life huh?)

I'm aware of the accrete's Firebird mirror site (http://www.accrete.com/fx-mirror/mt4...a-archives.htm) which has some versions but doesn't yet have v2.0.

Maybe that site could be updated and we could all point to it regularly. Or, maybe if I really get going with this EA I'll just go ahead and create the kind of site that I think is needed. But, with any creation comes an obligation to maintain (sort of like raising kids!).

They are identical in values. one has column A in scientific notation. Select all values in that column A and click Format in upper menu, then click Cells, then select Number tab, then select Number in Category pane, then set decimal to 0 and then click OK.

--- 帖子 #1602 ---
The problem with the date field is it that it is in unix format, or something. Google 'date/epoch converter'. The number you have is the number of seconds from Jan 1st 1970 00:00 hours. I have an excel formula that converts date to epoch, but not the otherway

Inserted Code  seconds from epoch = ((A3-25569)*86400)+(B3*3600)+(C3*60)+D3

where A = date in mm/dd/yyyy format

B = Hour

C = Minutes

D = Seconds

I think MQ4 has a built in converter as well, just have to look in the resource book.

Rusty

--- 帖子 #1634 ---
Traderone,

I don't know if this is the actual reason, I posted this today on the Phoenix thread.

As I feel most do, I use the present Strategy Tester and available data to help me develop EAs. Backtest bar data is basic OHLC data. LIve data would contain the interlace movements within each bar. Until LIve tick data is recorded, purchased or made available from Brokers, my confidence in Backtesting is moderate at best. As posted earlier, IBFX Broker plans to offer Live tick data in near fulture.

As important as I feel about using Live tick data to backtest, it is not my only concern. I also see difference from my Demo to Live results on several EAs, including Phoenix and Firebird. I've seen and have been told that after Demo charts are checked to confirm good entry points, that in Live trading more bad entry points are seen. I feel one reason is that Demo order execution is instant and Live trading can have delays many times between order request and order execution. One delay can be whether your Broker is providing tick data feeds direct or through a Trading Desk, and how they filter the data. Another reason is on low volume pairs, Live trades are not executed until minimum volume is accumulated. I don't know what is the minimum volume, but I have manually executed orders and they did not go though and FXDD advise this was the reason.

The slippage variable has no effect in Demo testing, but does on Live trading. Live trading can have either, if slippage too high, order execution to be many pips away from order request. Or miss the order completely, if slippage too low. You do not see these effects in Demo or backtest.

To try to summarize, I think using Live tick data for backtesting is critical, and at present, we will not see identical results between Demo and Live trading.

Everyone should ask their Broker if they have Live tick data feeds now for Strategy Tester. If not, do they plan to offer one soon. If someone finds a Broker providing Live tick data for MT4 Platform Strategy Tester, please post the Broker name.

Well, enough rambling on my part. Everyone have a great weekend.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #1688 ---
When UseMM=true, then Lots input is not functional. You need to change the Risk input to change lot size. Risk is percent of AccountEquity you want to risk per trade.

If you manually want to set lot size, then UseMM=false.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #1689 ---
1) What 'Risk' are you using, and what is the lot size that Firebird is trading with. ('percent' has to do with the channel Firebird uses to produce trade signals, not percent risk)

2) If you set MM to '0' or 'False' it will turn MM off, and then 'Lots' will be the number of lots Firebird will trade with.

If you decide to overide the MM and manually set lot size, start with .05 lots, and watch how it works for a couple of days. Once you are familiar with it, SLOWLY increase lot size. I would set 'pipstep' to 40, that way it wont open too many trades if the trend goes against you. Float is the killer here, negative float that is. I would set 'MaxOpenOrders' to something like 3, instead of the default of 10. At 3 orders you are already 80 to 120 pips away from the opening of the initial order, assuming a 'pipstep' of 40. it couild take a while for that pair to turn around and move 80 pips in your direction, and that could take a while, all along leaving you with -float. With a $300 account, you wont last long with a high -float. What is a high -float?? that I am not sure of yet. I currently have about 15% of my Account balance as negative float. I am not sure if that is too high or not, I would like to see it lower though, maybe someone else can chime in on their Float?? Good luck, I hope this helps

Rusty

ps Someone beat me to a reply

--- 帖子 #1712 ---
IMO, not only is it OK to disable Firebird as long as the reason is based on a pre-defined rule, but I think this type of intervention is entirely necessary.  I suppose most "rules" can be programmed in, but I lack the skills in that area.  In my case, I stop the EA when the open trade count reaches 12 to protect my core account.  Gotta live to fight another day...

I've been trading a live account with Firebird since 8/15 using the "old" V63G and basic settings of SL=300, TP=30, Pipstep=40, on 1 minute and recently 5 minute charts with the following pairs: USD/CAD, EUR/USD, and USD/CHF (since 10/26).  So far, the account is 131 wins and 3 losses, with 7 trades currently in float.

I also make extensive use of the "only short" and "only long" settings.  Newsflash everybody... Firebird WILL trade with the trend if you set it to.  It takes fewer trades overall, but IMO they're more reliable trades.

I never ever close trades manually, whether in profit or loss because I have not developed a good formula for doing so.  I've done some back testing on the "close everything on Friday" scenerio and results were very bad.  I also tested closing everything at the beginning of the month with poor results.  The best results by far were when I never manually closed any trades.  And I think manual intervention without a defined formula is a sign of undisciplined trading.  I have a formula for stopping firebird (12 trades), and I also have formulas for setting the "only long" and "only short" functions based on trend indicators that I am still testing.  I'm not trying to brag, just re-stating that discipline is the key to success in trading, whether it's with Firebird or some other system.

--- 帖子 #1713 ---
Thanks for the advice.  I think what you have stated is very well thought out and obviously tested.  I had not thought about the long only or short only option but I will consider it from now on.  I would have loved to catch this trend long instead of short.

--- 帖子 #1714 ---
Rusty,

The factor of 10 makes a considerable difference.  Consider for example the capital requirement, the number of currency pairs in your trading basket, the number of trades open at one time which of course impacts the margin requirement.  Currently, I'm working with one standard lot and up to five currency pairs which means as much as $5,000 in margin and as high as a couple of grand in float.   Psychologically, it's easier to walk away because you don't want to keep seeing those high negative floats!!

My theory is the settings we use successfully for mini accounts are in an inverse relationship to standard accounts so we would ratchet the settings down by some factor of "X".  My current settings, posted elsewhere in this thread, return 90%+ success, but when a trade goes bad, it really goes bad.

Also it may be that one of the earlier versions is better for standard lots (I don't understand why but it's possible), perhaps v.63gTS or even the "H" version.  I'm currently trading with v.2 and have not used the hedge version as of yet.

--- 帖子 #1743 ---
There is a bug in CheckJustCloseOrder() since the comment from closed order is followed with "[sl]" or "[tp]".  I fixed this bug and combine VG63H04-TSMM with v1.0a and v1.0c to get a new clean version.

MonoAutoSettings - ture to use Mono's daily range to calcuate tp, sl and pipstep

UseSafeArea - true to use the safe area from vg63h04

Hello guy´s,

I´m back again !

Last days was very terrible for our bird... mine on lost near 22% on live account, (use the H02 version with trailing stop on 5min TF, 2 minilot for every pair, EUR/USD, USD/CHF, CHF/JPY(best pair ever), EUR/GBP, EUR/CHF) but still up more than 120% since beginning in september...

Well not the latest Version, i know, but for me it works best and i see much people here lost more...

I thought long long times about how can we make this baby safer... In my oppinion the only way is to implement a slow martingale, not double every order but maybe encrease with the factor 1.5... so we can close all the orders at a small pullback and we don´t have to wait until price reaches the lowest TP Level from the first order...

Examlpe:

Now price is 1.1500... Bird goes short, price runs up to 1.1740... so if we had a pipstep from 40 now 8 orders are open and floating makes us ....

So let´s say we start with a half minilot, open the next order with 0,75 minilot, next with 1,13 minilot... and so on. Reduce pipstep to 30 pips and increase lotsize with the factor 1.5 (see pdf attached)

Only a 60 pips retracement are enough to close the orderblock postive (look pdf)...

That´s the only way we can make this baby safer in trending markets, now if the price runs 240 pips away it need a 240 pip retracement to close all orders, after 60 pips are enough...

Maybe there are some coders who can code this into the EA...

Thanks for your help !

mr.trader

That helps a lot for me to understand v1.0b.

Some of my thougts on firebird and 10point3.

10point3 is supposed to follow the trend at the very first entry, but ironically it usually ends up counter-trend. These two EAs also increase their positions when against the market, the difference is 10point3 is far more agressive. They all work best in the ranging market.

I think maybe the best thing for these two EAs to win, is to accept the loss at certain point in the big move, and start all over again. I read somewhere that trending market only accounts 30% of the time. The EAs will win as long as the profit made at 70% of market time exceeds the loss incurred in those 30% of market time by certain margin. I think some people have the feeling as well.

Just my two cents.

--- 帖子 #1758 ---
Hi,

I put some new changes in fb63vf03.

1)  Add SerialNo. If you want to restart a new FB but don't want to touch the  orders opened by the old EA, set the SeiralNo different from the old one.

2)  Add an advanced/regular trailing stop.  The old trailing stop only sets the stoploss 5 pips away the current market price once the market price goes away <TrailingStop> pips from the open price.  It would be easily hit due to the volatility.  Choose UseAdvanceTrailingStop would set the trailing stop in the normal behaviour, i.e., trailing stop will jump in <TrailingStop> pips.

3) Add Hedge option. Set UseHedge true for hedge option from v1.0b2.

I really doubt how much the hedge can help.  Can someone post the backtest result using hedge option?

--- 帖子 #1777 ---
I found this threat about a week ago and have spent some quality time with it so far. Since I am quite new in forex I do not know if my suggestions to improve the EA have any value at all. But since I do not want to be just a taker here it is.

I noticed this Friday during that big fall (USDSHF) around 08.30 that in left upper corner there was a remark - Trending Market DOWN. And for pair EURUSD around the same time it was remark - Trending Market UP.

So here is the question can we use those remarks? And the answer to I think we can since the remark was created by EA.

So can we but a little code to EA that when the signal is:

• Trending Market DOWN then the EA will initiate SELL trade

• Trending Market UP then the EA will initiate Buy trade.

Those trades would have two termination criteria:

1. Standard ST and TP (according to settings everybody use)

2. Trade is active until the signal about market trend is active

Those trades will stay open until one of the parameters (witch ever comes first) mentioned before is met.

So that was my idea how to reduce losses trending market.

--- 帖子 #1800 ---
Traderlismiss, et al:

I have been testing FB for about 6+ months.  Both live & demo.  As we know FB does horrible in a trend and hits SL causing massive losses.  I have found that v 63H04TS_MM, does the best job, but it needs to close trades after five days.  As stated in the preface ~ 90+% of trades close in profit within the first five days.  I was in the process of doing this and was making progress, when the latest trend hit over Thanksgiving.  None of my trades was older than 5 days, most only 2 days old, but I still got stopped out during the night while I was asleep and lost about 30%.

I have been reading about the Goblin EA on TSD Forex and have just loaded it tonight.  It looks at Daily Trends and determines whether they are strong or weak and in which direction.  If the trend is strongly up, you buy only on the dips; if the trend is ranging/weak downtrend/weak uptrend, you can buy or sell; or if the trend is strongly down, you sell only on the rallies.

If something like this could be incorporated into the envelope of the EA, so that it would always be looking at the overall trend, it might prevent a sudden calamity.  The other thing that might help reduce losses is that if the EA senses a strong trend, that it automatically closes all positions until the more ranging scenario returns, thus preventing the EA to run the full amount of the SL.

This in combination with a reduced number of pairs open, pairs to be closed after 5 days, and then incorporating the ideas above.  Any programmers game for tackling this?

1Trader2

--- 帖子 #1801 ---

--- 帖子 #1802 ---
Firebird has one of the better trend analyzer (iFXAnalyzer) already coded in the EA. It is just not used. Using this trend analyzer can help to not enter repeated PipStep orders during wrong direction sustained trends. But also there must be method to exit orders that have been caught up in wrong trend direction before they reach max stoploss. This will reduce the number of trades and there can be several days of no trading during strong trends. While running Ea on M1, M5, M15 or M30, the trend analyzer should be based on higher timeframe (H1,H4 or D1) to better indicate sustained trends.

I'm not aware of any trend indicator code that is 100% correct, or even near it. There will be occasional false trend indications that either prematurely exits existing order or does not enter order at an acceptable point. Overall, profit growth might be slowed down, but may be more consistent over time.

Just a few thoughts.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #1812 ---
Fellow Traders and Traderettes,

I think it comes as no deep revelation that FireBird is one of many trading tools available.  It works best during ranging markets, not trending markets (again no deep revelation).

If Forex is alive and dynamic, why trade with the same static strategy?  When I terminated FireBird last week at the beginning of the trend, I initiated something else.  For example, Sidus and Bagovino are both good trend strategies.  So when seasons change and it's freezing cold/raining/snow, you don't dress in beachwear.  You change clothes and dress appropriately for the season (if you don't then this message doesn't apply to you!).

Ranging markets will return again, just as sure as the spring thaw comes every year.  So cut your losses and shut 'er down during trends until we develop a trend-detection method, be it Goblin or some other tool.  And don't cry over evaporated funds; focus instead on the profit you'll make next trade.

Adapt.  Improvise.  Dominate.

--- 帖子 #1815 ---
Now let's do a comparison of goblin or and a potentially improved firebird.

What is goblin? It is an upgrade of 10point3. It is a hybrid of martingale method with trend detection. Once the ea is launched, it enters a position in the direction of 1h trend, as long as the 1h trend is not against a strong 4h or daily trend.

Suppose firebird is equipped with the same martingale method, and the same trend detection system, also follows the rule that positions are entered in the direction of 1 h trend, when 1h trend is not against a strong 4h/daily. But firebird is intrinsically more selective in openning a trade, it tries to buy on dip and sell on rally from its very birth. Therefore, in theory this improved firebird should be safer than goblin, supposing everything else is the same.

Of course, goblin is subject to further test as well although seems very promising. My point is firebird still has a lot of room to improve itself. I might be right, and might be wrong.

The above comparison is just for making a point. No disrespect to goblin and its author bluto at all. Actually I am very gratefull for bluto's kindness of sharing his excellent work.

teamfri,

You make an excellent point and it seems promising (if not a complex programming question). I'm not up to speed on Goblin just yet but I know FireBird is outstanding in ranging markets. Many testimonials (live and demo) on micro and mini and standard accounts confirm this point.

But...as you say Goblin requires further testing. That brings me to the Noob, demam_emas as set forth below:

Bagovino is a great trend strategy, again confirmed by many testimonials, live and demo yada, yada, yada. Using bags last week, you would have made hundreds of pips on the cable uptick. It's a simple ma cross confirmed by rsi(14), although Bagovino enthusiasts may insist on rsi(21) with fibs and retracements...kewl. In any event, it works in trending markets.

demam_emas recommends incorporating bags as the lead signal so for example, when bags signals a bearish trend, FireBird would open only short trades. Recognizing full well that FireBird is a counter-trend system, we would force-feed the Bird, so to speak, to only allow shorts or alternatively establish a hedge, until we confirm the bear trend. Once confirmed (based on x number of candles) shorts are allowed and the hedge cancels the long. Moving SL to BE after perhaps 10-15 pips would lock in profit just in case bags gave a false trend signal. Just reverse the foregoing in case of a bull trend. Obviously the hedge would still cost a few pips but it would be much less than the cost we incur now going to SL.

Collaborative effort ladies and gentlemen. Please criticize, question, tear this apart. But I think it makes sense and moves in the direction of the trend we want.

Adapt. Improvise. Dominate.

--- 帖子 #1820 ---
I've been following trends with Firebird in my live account since mid October. Given today's price action, I hope everyone has been applying some kind of trend analysis to this EA. It's not rocket science (i think I've said that before...). Just pick a few of your favorite MA's and make a decision when they cross.

There has been a comment or two that "force feeding" (props to Monema$ter  for the term) Firebird might result in too few trades opening to cover the inevitable losses when a trend changes direction. My information indicates otherwise. For example, I don't think anyone would disagree that the USD/CHF has been in a bear trend since October. I began trading the pair in my live Firebird account on 11/6 with the EA set to "only short". Since then, 17 USD/CHF trades have closed for profit. No losses and no trades currently open on that pair. So, it seems that pullbacks during a trend are sufficient to trigger a reasonable number of profitable trades.

--- 帖子 #1826 ---
Attached is Firebird-v3.0.

In an attempt to minimize bad effect of strong up or down market movements, I have coded a new Firebird to use iFXAnalyzer as an up and down strong trend indicator. The EA will not place trades during strong up or down trends indicated by chart message "Market Trending up" or "Market Trending Down". I added a Hedge function option to place reverse trade when PipStep trade is triggered. Hedge orders have ability to increase lot size. I cleaned up the EA and now there are no warnings when compiled in MetaEditor. Other added functions are described below. UseEquityProtection -if true, close all orders when negative Float is excessvie. FloatPercent –percent of balance for equity protection. UseMM-money management. Risk-pecent of account equity to risk per trade. MaxOpenOrders-sets maximum number of open trades at same time. MinMarginLevel-below minimum Margin Level percent % trading stops. CloseDays-number of days trade is open before auto closing. LossLevel-loss amount before auto closing after Closedays. UseHedge-if true, places reverse order with PipStep order. HedgeLotFactor-hedge order Lots will be increased by this factor. HedgeTakeProfit- HedgeStopLoss- AutoCal-if true, iRSI() calculation of TakeProfit, StopLoss and PipStep. (not hedge orders) This Firebird, as well as most other versions, is very slow in backtest. I can assure the added EA functions work. In backtest with default settings, it performed well on eurusd. gbpusd backtest was a bit shakey, but still in profit. I have not tested other pairs. I hope it performs well in Demo and Live accounts. I found better profits when HedgeLotFactor is set between 2-4.

Warning: The success or failure of this Expert Advisor is the exclusive responsibility of the Enduser.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #1838 ---
I 've been following goblin closely for quite a few days, and the discussion there really made me think a lot.

Personally, I think goblin is still not a real trend following system, but very much an EA with martingale method playing the main role, and I made a suggestion to transform it into a true trend following system with martingale method playing a supporting role.

I think for firebird, it would also be good to transform it into a daily trend following system. We could let it follow the daily trend by using whatever indicator we feel comfortable with. We only buy in an uptrend and sell in a downtrend. And in the daily trend, there must be minor trends against it, which firebird can take advantage of them by using its strength of  'buy on dip and sell on rally'.

A daily uptrend and downtrend usually lasts a few days, firebird should be good in this period. The drawdown would be the potential loss incurred at the transional period, the period market changes from bull to bear, or from bear to bull, or in the daily sideway market. Shall we cut our existing positions when there is a signal of direction change of daily trend? I think only when the averaging loss reached certain level. If we cut them too early, we might suffer in a typical sideway market. If we cut too late, we will be against a big move.

For this idea, I am really not sure about its possibility of success. Just for you guys to see if it is worth trying.

--- 帖子 #1839 ---
Glenn,

How many orders were opened?

If UseMM=true, the lot size is a calculation based on Risk% of AccountEquity. If lot size is larger than you want, reduce Risk %.

Example:

AccountEquity = $10,000

Risk=10;

Then Lots will be 1.0 for 1st trade. 1st Hedge trade Lot size is Lots * HedgeLotFactor. In same example, if HedgeLotFactor=3, then 1st Hedge trade will have Lots = 3.0. For same lot size on both normal and Hedge, set HedgeLotFactor=1.

If UseMM=false, then you manually set the Lots variable to whatever lot size you want. Hedge lot calculation is same as above.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #1843 ---
As requested by Michaelw, I have coded a Trade Time scheduler into latest Firebird v3.0. It is a little bit of overkill. But, it will allow to schedule up to 4 "Trading Time" zones per day and a full week's schedule to be set at one time.

If UseTradeScheduler=true, then the following applies.

Each "Trading Time" zone 1 through 4 has a Start and an End for each day.

To trade all day , set "day"...Start1=0 and "day"...End4=24. This is needed for each trading day.

To skip a full day, set "day"...Start1=0 and "day"...End4=0.

Note: EA is coded to use your Local PC Time.

Here is a Monday example.

MonTradeHourStart1 = 0; - (Trading Time zone 1 start)

MonTradeHourEnd1 = 8; - (Trading Time zone 1 end)

MonTradeHourStart2 = 10;

MonTradeHourEnd2 = 16;

MonTradeHourStart3 = 18;

MonTradeHourEnd3 = 20;

MonTradeHourStart4 = 22;

MonTradeHourEnd4 = 24;

In above schedule, EA trades from 00:00 (midnight) to 08:00, then from 10:00 to 16:00, then from 18:00 to 20:00, then from 22:00 to 24:00.

Non-Trading Time is from 08:00 to 10:00, then from 16:00 to 18:00, then from 20:00 to 22:00.

Wackena

After orders have been opened, then premature Hedge orders should stop. I will investigate a fix.

--- 帖子 #1853 ---
For the 2 lots and 6 lots orders. You have either turned off UseMM and set Lots=2. Or, UseMM=true, and default settings, Risk=5% and AccountEquity equals or is near $45,000. In either case, the HedgeFactor=3 and that is why the 2nd order was for 6 lots.

Just had another double order on usdchf. Reason unknown, still investigating. It may not be a prolblem . Time will tell.

I started my FDXX $3000 demo 2006.12.03 on 4 pairs-eurusd, gbpusd, usdjpy, usdchf. EquityProtection was set at 10% of balance. This only allows a $300 negative float. Last night had 2 orders closed for loses when negative FLoat was more than 10% limit. EquityProtection feature works. On my $3000 demo, I have now set FloatPercent=20 (20% of Balance=~$600 for negative float limit). Users should periodically re-evaluate their FloatPercent setting to assure, based on your Balance, you allow enough negative float for Firebird to work. While if EA is profitable, adjust FLoatPercent down to protect balance.

Another suggestion is to turn Equity Protection off and let EA run for awhile to see average Float p/l and then set FloatPercent accordingly to level of protection you want.

int MagicfromSymbol() { // included by Renato

return(MagicNumber);

--- 帖子 #1866 ---
MoneyMa$ter,

Just recently, MetaQuotes (MQL4) made CurTime() and LocalTime() obsolete and replaced them with TimeCurrent() and TimeLocal(). http://docs.mql4.com/obsolete

I think the MetaEditor in your SB account is an older version and does not have these changes in the Compile reference. You could try to update to build 200 and hopefully these errors will stop.

NOTE: To All:

Please make sure you use latest MT4 Platform build 200 with this EA. If using older version, EA time routines could fail to function.

MoneyMa$ter, thanks for the heads up.

--- 帖子 #1867 ---
nvwine,

I see similar hedge order openings as you report. This is the way I hoped this EA would work. The Hedge Order call is controlled by PipStep call and MaxOpenOrders setting. On call for PipStep order, a Hedge Order is also called. The number of Hedge orders is controlled by MaxOpenOrders setting. Example: if MaxOpenOrders=5:

1st order is normal EA call.

2nd normal order and 1st Hedge Order are on 1st PipStep call.

3rd normal order and 2nd Hedge Order are on 2nd PipStep call.

I think what is happening is if 1st Hedge order closes before 3rd normal order is open, it throws the  complete sequence off. I will investigate the sequence this weekend.

Wackena

Firebird 3.2

Broker FXDD - eurusd, gbpusd, usdjpy, usdchf

Deposit $3,000

Timeframe M5

Balance $5,120

Equity $4,779

Wins 72 - Loses 7

Open Orders 4 (Float p/l $-340)

ROI 25.9 %

Started test on 2006.12.03.

I had 7 loses, that were my fault. They comprised of 2 groups, 1st for 2 loses and 2nd for 5 loses. 1st group was when I started the test and had PercentFloatLevel=10. This only allows negative Float to be 10% of Balance before it closes all orders. 2nd group of loses was when I broke a basic rule of never working on a code if EA is running. I set the equity proctection level again too low and it closed all open orders again. you can see none of the loses were sl loses. If I hadn't made these 2 miistakes, I should be up even more by a few hundred dollars with no loses.

This doesn't it mean that Firebird 3.2 won't blowup sometime in the future, but it survived the NFP news on Friday. The Hedge orders seem to be very useful in making profits during both trend directions. We will need to wait and see a few major trend spikes before we know if this EA can play and not get hurt too bad in the real world.

Firebird is a counter trend EA and needs a range of negative float to perform as designed. I suggest that PercentFloatLevel setting be set to allow ~$1,000 per each lot for negative float. Example: 1 lot = ten orders of 0.1 lot. To protect equity, PercentFloatLevel needs to be adjusted as equity increases. On equity increases, PercentFloatLevel can be set lower to maintain necessary amount for negative float.

I can not over state the importance of protecting your equity when running Firebird EAs. It's history has been to make real impressive profits over time, just to see it quickly get wipe out in only a few days. Use the equity protection, trading time filter, manual observations or whatever it takes.

Wackena

--- 帖子 #1887 ---
The hedge orders should be triggered along with PipStep orders. For some reason, part of the original Firebird code that tracks open orders gets confused and loses track sometimes of 1 to 2 orders. As stated this part of the original code and I will investigate possible fix.

The concern I have had with all Firebird versions is its inability to handle long sustained trends. It likes long ranging markets that moves within a 300 to 500 pips range, It's true that FB3.2 with the hedge feature does better, but it also has this same problem. When we have long sustained trends like we are having now on the 4 major pairs, FB is going to get caught with open orders that keep drifting toward the StopLoss. This is usually seen after a few days and you see 1 or 2 orders on a chart that has been open for a few days. The Stoploss could be set at 500 and this would only delay the inevitable loss.

Well with that being said, I think FB needs a routine to close all orders, on a pair, when the sum of all orders are in profit. With FB3.2 present default settings, Hedge orders lots are 3 times higher than standard order lot size. This should allow a point in time where the Hedge profit minus all open orders is still a profit. I think this should be a turn on - turn off function and it will be up to the user to determine if in long trending or long ranging market.

Wackena

This may not be the appropriate place to say this, but to anyone looking at this EA who doesn't have a significant amount of Forex experience, please be careful!!

Firebird in the hands of a new trader is like a 600 HP sports car in the hands of a kid.  It'll go like hell for block or so... till it hits a pole.  But try telling a kid they're better off with an econobox...

This EA is *FAR* from being a fully automated system that you simply set and forget.  Regardless of version, it is a tool that requires a great deal of caution and market savvy to use correctly as many people on this thread have learned over the last 2 months.

--- 帖子 #1921 ---
I agree with you that risk can't be totally avoided and is part of the game.

But my personal opinion is that float should always be kept at a minimum.

1] Because it gives a better starting point for conditions when trends really get out of hand.

2] Even when the huge float turns into winners it doesn't mean it's very profiteble. If the money wasn't tied up you could possibly have made several winning smaller trades.

3] Huge float earns less when you follow RM/MM rules.

4] The money you set aside to buffer the huge DD that occure once every 100 trades means that that money isn't earning in 99 trades. But smart MM/RM can improve that situation to some extend.

More on Risk Management and Money Management.

MM/RM is no fix. It's a magnifying glass.

It fools you when testing. It hides the real system performance.

A system should be profiteble without MM/RM. Only then start using RM/MM

MM/RM is not just scaling a few lots as seen in most EAs (but soem MM is a very good start). It's a real art that can get very complex. But it has great advantage. Not only safty wise but also speeding up portfolio growth. There is a lot of info to be found on MM/RM. If you can't find any you can start looking here http://www.adaptrade.com/Articles/article-op.htm Also play with their program. It's awsome.

Also read a bit about Sharpe and/or Sortino Ratio.

It will learn you that decent MM/RM punishes you for having a system with a huge DD. It cuts down the max. allowed lots because it keeps being paranoid about the possibility of the DD.

As an example a huge DD system (with massive gains if it reverses) is allowed to trade 5 lots and and a system that just keeps collecting a few pips in many short lasting trades may be allowed to trade 15 lots just because it feels/is so safe.

So the 'smooth system' collects 3x more $ per pip earned.

--- 帖子 #1929 ---
Today, January 9, 2007, FireBird v2[1] with MM, TS generated 37 pips profit in Eur/Aud. I initiated FireBird today because cable was ranging, just as referenced in the post quoted above.

Perhaps too simplistic but this is the third time, and while still statistically insignificant in that 3 robins don't make a spring, we're still getting warmer. Theory is as long as cable is ranging, then it's safer to use FireBird as you're less likely to see those strong market trends that kill the bird. I've only applied this theory to Eur/Aud but it should work for the majors also because if cable ranges, the majors should follow.

--- 帖子 #1946 ---
In my opinion:

EA's are trading tools. Firebird is a great tool for a specific set of market conditions. I wouldn't use a wrench to hammer a nail...  I increased my live account 50% with this tool, and I held on to my gains. Not bragging... I'm sure many traders did better with it than I did, but they're probably tired of hearing the same old complaints after repeated warnings. Anyone who studies this thread will see that it is rife with cautionary posts about the fact that this EA is not for inexperienced traders. Does that make it a "bad" program? No.

In fact, I don't believe new traders should waste their time with EA's at all for at least the first year or two. All the same rules apply to profitable manual trading. Learn to trade manually (and profitably) before working on anything like this. Retail Forex vendors don't provide Metatrader with it's automated trading capabilities because they think it will make traders more money. Going back to the tool analogy... if someone hasn't learned to effectively use a hand saw yet, then they'll make a bloody mess with a power saw.

--- 帖子 #1955 ---
I agreee 100% with you on that. V63-TS is a great little EA, but it does need supervision. It has poor open trade management. There have been attempts, by others, to impliment some sort of trade management that would close lossing trades if they were x days old, and too far into the wrong side. Firebird has a routein that averages the take profit level when it opens more then one trade. This is so that when the price retraces a little all the open trades close at once, then FB can open a new set of trades. I haven't seen this implimented yet, so I am not sure it is profitable, or if it even works. I have looked at it, but I am not up to the programing task.

--- 帖子 #1959 ---
Yes, Firebird 3.2 includes hedging. To know the logics, just read the comments inside the code when you open de .mq4 file with the MetaEditor.

Inserted Code UseHedge = true;  // Places reverse order with PipStep order.
HedgeLotFactor = 1;     // Hedge order Lots will be increase by this factor.
HedgeTakeProfit= 30;
HedgeStoploss = 100;

--- 帖子 #1963 ---
The last version that I coded is Firebird 3.2 and is attached. Other versions are located here.
http://www.accrete.com/fx-mirror/mt4-firebird/

I've found out the hard way that Firebird (any version) will lose money if not manually controlled when needed. FB is a reverse trend EA in that it waits till price reaches either upper band and enters sell order or lower band to enter buy order. The concept is that the price will eventually reverse to take profit. Before it reverses, PipStep orders will be placed while price continues to move up (Sell PipStep orders) or down (Buy PipStep orders). If the trend continues, the 300 pips Stoploss gives possibility of many PipStep orders. This can lead to high DrawDowns. You much decide if trend is worth staying in or manually close order/s for small lost. Also, in most instances, the price never reverses enough to close all orders in profit. So you much also decide when to close a long term open order.

This is experience only, no set rules. If you can learn when to stay in and when to get out, this EA can make profits as I have run 3.2 in profit for several months.

The hedge function places both Buy and Sell orders when PipStep order is called. I've found this improves profits, but will also have more occurrences where manually intervention is needed.

The MA_timeframe=15 and I have not changed this. On M5 chart selection, you will have more orders and higher DrawDowns. Lately I use M30 chart selection and it seems to slow down number of trades and reduced high DrawDowns. I think M30 predicts trends better.

The EquityProtection feature in 3.2 is not the best code. Setting the Float Percent correctly needs to be constantly changed in relation to Account Balance, and so, I don't use it.

Wackena

Percent=0.10000000

slip=100

Lots=1.00000000

TakeProfit=30

Stoploss=300

Fast_Period=23

Fast_Price=1

Slow_Period=84

Slow_Price=1

DivergenceLimit=0.00200000

Use_V63D_Divergence=1

PipStep=30

IncreasementType=0.00000000

DVLimit=10

PipsGoal=500

PipsLoss=500

GMT=0

DST=0

OpeningHour=0

ClosingHour=23

writelog=0

--- 帖子 #2008 ---
You can include the set files using the manage attachments button below the text entry window when making a post. Since you can't attach the *.set extension you can either change the extension to *.txt or place the *.set file in a zip file. The *.txt file is confusing to some people so be sure to point out they need to change the extension back to *.set in order to use it in the preset directory.
